Follower's Recitation Behind the Imam: Hanafi Proofs
Hanafi proof that the follower does not recite behind the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the follower's recitation behind the imam and cite the four textual proofs (Quran and hadith).

Core Idea
The imam's recitation suffices for the follower; silence is mandatory.

In congregational prayer, the follower (muqtadi) is required to follow the imam. A key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools is whether the follower recites the Quran during audible prayers. This lesson presents the Hanafi position with its textual proofs from the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Begin by identifying the Hanafi ruling: the follower does not recite behind the imam; it is makruh tahrimi to do so.
2
Analyze the primary proof (Qur'an)
Examine Surah al-A'raf 7:204 which commands listening and silence when the Qur'an is recited. How does this apply to the imam's recitation?
3
Analyze the three hadith proofs
Review the hadith from Abu Hurairah (be silent when imam recites), Imran ibn Husayn (Prophet's disapproval), and Jabir (imam's recitation is recitation for the follower). Understand how each supports the ruling.
4
Understand the opposing view and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school argues from the general command to recite Fatihah. The Hanafi response is that the specific commands to be silent take precedence, and the imam's recitation fulfills the follower's obligation.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: in Hanafi, the follower remains silent; in Shafi'i, the follower must recite Fatihah. This affects validity and sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يقرأ المؤتم خلف الامام. ... (1) آيت میں ہے: واذا قرئ القرآن فاستمعوا له وانصتوا لعلكم ترحمون (الاعراف 204). (2) عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: انما جعل الامام ليؤتم به فاذا كبر فكبروا واذا قرأ فانصتوا. (3) عن عمران بن حصين ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى الظهر فجعل رجل يقرأ خلفه سبح اسم ربك الاعلى فلما انصرف قال: ايكم قرأ او ايكم القارئ؟ فقال رجل: انا. فقال: قد ظننت ان بعضكم خالجنيها. (4) عن جابر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من كان له امام فقراءة الامام له قراءة.
The follower does not recite behind the imam. ... (1) The verse says: 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent that you may receive mercy.' (2) From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is appointed to be followed; when he says takbir, say takbir, and when he recites, be silent.' (3) From Imran ibn Husayn: The Messenger of Allah prayed Zuhr, and a man recited behind him 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la'. When he finished, he said: 'Which of you recited?' The man said: 'I did.' He said: 'I thought that some of you were contending with me.' (4) From Jabir: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the imam is recitation for him.'
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling that the follower (muqtadi) does not recite the Quran during prayer when behind an imam. The author provides four proofs. First, Quranic evidence: Surah al-A'raf 204 commands listening and silence when the Quran is recited. The imam's recitation in prayer falls under this command, so the follower must listen and remain silent. Second, a hadith from Abu Hurairah where the Prophet explicitly says that when the imam recites, the followers should be silent. Third, a hadith from Imran ibn Husayn showing that the Prophet disapproved of a follower reciting behind him, indicating it is improper. Fourth, a hadith from Jabir stating that the imam's recitation counts as the follower's recitation. Therefore, the follower's own recitation is not required; it is even disliked (makruh) to recite behind the imam. This is a distinctive Hanafi position; other schools (Shafi'i) require the follower to recite Surah al-Fatihah even behind the imam.

Key Terms
مؤتم (mu'tamm): The person following the imam in congregational prayer
قراءة الامام (qira'at al-imam): The recitation of the imam is considered as the recitation of the followers

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which verse does the Hanafi school primarily use to prove that the follower should not recite behind the imam?
A) 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' (al-Muzzammil 20)
B) 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent' (al-A'raf 204)
C) 'And stand before Allah in devout obedience' (al-Baqarah 238)
D) 'And whoever recites a verse, for him is a good deed' (al-An'am 160)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the follower does not recite behind the imam; the imam's recitation counts as the follower's recitation, based on Quranic command and prophetic instructions.

Two Intentions Required for Following an Imam
Ruling on the necessity of two intentions when following an imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two intentions required when following an imam according to the Hanafi school and identify the consequence of omitting the intention to follow.

Core Idea
To follow an imam, you must intend both the prayer and the following — the imam is your guarantor.

The source passage clarifies that simply standing behind an imam with a general prayer intention is insufficient. The Hanafi school, based on the hadith 'The imam is a guarantor,' requires a specific intention to follow that particular imam. Understanding this ruling ensures the validity of your congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act in question
The act is 'joining another's prayer' (iqtida) - praying as a follower behind an imam.
2
List the two required intentions
First, intention of the specific prayer being offered (e.g., Zuhr, Asr). Second, intention of following that particular imam.
Both must be present simultaneously.
3
Understand the reason
The imam is a 'damin' (guarantor) for the follower's prayer, taking responsibility for its correctness. This necessitates a conscious connection via intention.
The hadith directly supports this concept.
4
Note the consequence of omission
If one omits the intention to follow the imam, the iqtida does not take effect. The person prays alone, even though physically standing behind the imam.
The prayer remains valid as an individual prayer, but not as a congregation.
5
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'The imam is a guarantor, and the mu'adhdhin is a trustee.' From this, the Hanafi school derives that the follower must intend to be under the imam's guarantee.
This is a zanni al-thubut hadith, but decisive in the school's reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۲۴] (۵۴) ومن اراد الدخول فى صلوة غيره يحتاج الى نيتين نية الصلوة ونية الامام. کوئی آدمی دوسرے کی اقتدا کر رہا ہو تو اس کو دو قسموں کی نیت کرنی ہوگی۔ ایک اصل نماز پڑھنے کی نیت اور دوسری امام کی اقتدا کرنے کی نیت۔
(۱) کیونکہ امام مقتدی کی نماز کا ضامن ہے اصلاح اور فساد میں۔ اس لئے اس کی اقتدا کرنے کی بھی نیت کرنی ہوگی۔ اگر اس کی اقتدا کرنے کی نیت نہیں کی اور صف میں کھڑے ہو کر اصل نماز کی نیت کی تو اقتدا نہیں ہوگی (۲) عن ابی ھریر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الامام ضامن والمؤذن مؤتمن (و) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء ان الامام ضامن و المؤذن مؤتمن ص ۵۱ نمبر ۲۰۷) اس سے معلوم ہوا
[224] (54) Whoever intends to enter into another's prayer needs two intentions: the intention of the prayer and the intention of following the imam. When a person is following another, he must make two types of intention: one intention of performing the original prayer, and the second intention of following the imam. (1) Because the imam is a guarantor (damin) for the follower's prayer in terms of validity and corruption. Therefore, one must also intend to follow him. If one does not intend to follow but stands in the row and intends the original prayer, then following does not occur. (2) From Abu Hurairah: the Messenger of Allah said, 'The imam is a guarantor, and the mu'adhdhin is a trustee.' (Tirmidhi). From this it is understood.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a person who wishes to pray behind an imam (joining another's prayer) requires two simultaneous intentions: (1) the intention of the specific prayer (e.g., Zuhr, Asr), and (2) the intention of following that particular imam. The reason given is that the imam is a 'damin' (guarantor) for the follower's prayer—he takes responsibility for its correctness. Therefore, the follower must consciously connect himself to the imam from the start. If one merely lines up and intends the prayer without intending to follow, the iqtida (following) does not take effect; the person would be praying alone, even if physically standing behind an imam. The proof is a hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'The imam is a guarantor, and the mu'adhdhin is a trustee.' This supports the idea that the imam bears responsibility, necessitating an explicit intention to follow. This ruling applies to all congregational prayers where following an imam is valid (except for Janaazah prayer which has different rules).

Key Terms
نية الصلوة ونية الامام (niyyat al-salah wa niyyat al-imam): Two simultaneous intentions: (1) the specific prayer being offered, (2) the act of following that particular imam.
ضامن (damin): The imam is a guarantor for the validity of the follower's prayer, meaning he takes responsibility for its correctness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a person stands behind an imam intending the prayer but without intending to follow him?
A) His prayer is valid as a follower.
B) His prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) He is considered to be praying alone, not as a follower.
D) His intention is automatically corrected by his action.

Key Takeaway
Intention to follow the imam is a necessary condition for congregational prayer in the Hanafi school; without it, the follower is considered to be praying alone.

Muqtadi's Intention and the Fatiha Behind the Imam Debate
Ruling on muqtadi's intentions and inter-madhhab dispute on Fatiha recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two intentions required for a muqtadi and compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i/Maliki positions on reciting Fatiha behind the imam, citing the key proofs.

Core Idea
The muqtadi must intend both the prayer and to follow the imam; the imam's recitation suffices for the follower's Fatiha obligation.

This lesson explores two interconnected rulings from the Hanafi tradition: first, the requirement for a follower to make two intentions when joining congregational prayer, and second, the debated question of whether the follower must recite Fatiha behind the imam. The passage presents the Hanafi position supported by hadith, then addresses the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the muqtadi's intention requirements
The text states that a muqtadi needs two intentions: one for the specific prayer (e.g., Zuhr) and one for following the imam (iqtida'). The hadith 'al-imam dhamin' (the imam is a guarantor) is cited as proof.
Without the intention to follow, the prayer is not considered congregational.
2
State the Hanafi position on reciting Fatiha behind the imam
The Hanafi school holds that the imam's recitation suffices for the muqtadi; the muqtadi does not recite Fatiha in loud or silent prayers.
This is supported by hadith of Abu Darda and the practice of Ibn 'Umar.
3
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik require the muqtadi to recite Fatiha behind the imam in all prayers, citing the hadith of 'Ubada: 'There is no prayer for one who does not recite the Fatiha.'
This hadith is general and interpreted by Hanafis as applying to individuals not in congregation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis agree that Fatiha is wajib, but argue that the imam's recitation fulfills it for the muqtadi. They cite the hadith that the imam is a guarantor (dhamin) and note that even the Shafi'is agree in the case of a latecomer joining in ruku'.
Imam Muhammad recommends precautionary recitation in silent prayers according to some narrations.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In Hanafi practice, the muqtadi remains silent behind the imam; in Shafi'i/Maliki practice, the muqtadi recites Fatiha, especially in silent prayers.
This difference affects daily congregational worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاوّل) كتاب الصلوة [۲۲۴ (۵۴) ومن اراد الدخول فى صلوة غيره يحتاج الى نيتين نية الصلوة ونية امام ص ۳۲۱ نمبر ۱۲۲۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام نے فاتحہ پڑھ لی تو گویا کہ مقتدی نے بھی پڑھ لی وہ بغیر فاتحہ کے نہ رہے (۵) عن ابی درداء سمعه يقول سئل رسول الله الله في كل صلوة قراءة ؟ قال نعم قال رجل من الانصار وجبت هذه؟ فالتفت الى وكنت اقرب القوم منه فقال ما ارى الامام اذا ام القوم الا قد كفا هم (الف) (نسائی شریف، باب اكتفاء الماموم بقراءة الامام ص ۰۷ انمبر ۹۲۴ / دار قطنی ص ۳۲۶ نمبر ۱۲۴۸) اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مقتدیوں کو امام کی قرآت کافی ہے (۶) موطا امام مالک میں ہے كان عبد الله بن عمر لا يقرأ خلف الامام (ب) (موطا امام مالک، باب ترک القراءة خلف الامام فیما جهر ص ۶۸) (۷) مقتدی رکوع میں امام کے ساتھ ملے تو تو مقتدی کو وہ رکعت مل گئی۔ لیکن فاتحہ پڑھنے کا موقع نہیں ملا تو گویا کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک بھی اس صورت میں امام کا پڑھا ہوا فاتحہ مقتدی کے لئے کافی ہو گیا تو آخر ایک صورت میں وہ بھی حنفیوں کے ساتھ ہو گئی۔

امام شافعی، امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ امام کے پیچھے فاتحہ پڑھے گا۔ چاہے قرآت جہری کر رہا ہو یا سری۔ اور ایک روایت ہے کہ سری قرآت کر رہا ہو تو قرآت فاتحہ کرے گا اور جہری کر رہا ہو تو نہیں کرے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبادة بن صامت ان رسول الله قال لا صلوة لمن لم يقرء بفاتحة الكتاب (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب وجوب القراءة للامام والماموم في الصلوات کلھافى الحضر والسفر وما گھر فیها و ما تخافت ص ۱۰۴ نمبر ۷۵۶ مسلم شریف، باب وجوب قراءة الفاتحۃ فی کل رکعته ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۳۹۴ را بو داؤد شریف نمبر ۸۲۳) اس حدیث سے ثابت کرتے ہیں کہ مقتدی کے لئے بھی فاتحہ پڑھنا ضروری ہے۔ جواب : حنفیہ بھی فاتحہ واجب کرتے ہیں لیکن مقتدی کی جانب سے امام نے پڑھ لیا اس لئے مقتدی کی جانب سے کافی ہو گیا۔ جیسے کہ پہلے احادیث سے ثابت کیا گیا۔ امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ احادیث کی بنا پر سری نماز میں احتیاط فا تحہ پڑھ لے ( ہدایہ اولین فصل فی القراءة ص ۱۰۱) [۲۲۴] (۵۴) جس نے دوسرے کی نماز میں داخل ہونے کا ارادہ کیا و محتاج ہے دو نیتوں کا نماز کی نیت کا اور اتباع کی نیت کا۔ کوئی آدمی دوسرے کی اقتدا کر رہا ہو تو اس کو دو قسموں کی نیت کرنی ہوگی۔ ایک اصل نماز پڑھنے کی نیت اور دوسری امام کی اقتدا کرنے کی نیت۔ (۱) کیونکہ امام مقتدی کی نماز کا ضامن ہے اصلاح اور فساد میں۔ اس لئے اس کی اقتدا کرنے کی بھی نیت کرنی ہوگی۔ اگر اس کی اقتدا کرنے کی نیت نہیں کی اور صف میں کھڑے ہو کر اصل نماز کی نیت کی تو اقتدا نہیں ہوگی (۲) عن ابی ھریر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الامام ضامن والمؤذن مؤتمن (و) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء ان الامام ضامن و المؤذن مؤتمن ص ۵۱ نمبر ۲۰۷) اس سے معلوم ہوا حاشیہ : (الف) آپ سے پوچھا گیا کیا ہر نماز میں قرآت ہے؟ آپ نے فرمایا ہاں ! انصار کے ایک آدمی نے کہا یہ قرآت واجب ہوگئی تو حضور میری طرف متوجہ ہوئے اور میں آپ سے قوم میں سے زیادہ قریب میں تھا۔ آپ نے فرمایا میں نہیں سمجھتا ہوں مگر یہ کہ امام نے قوم کی امامت کی تو ان کی قرآت ان کو کافی ہوگی (ب) عبد اللہ بن عمر امام کے پیچھے قرآت نہیں کرتے تھے (ج) آپ نے فرمایا اس کی نماز ہی نہیں جس نے سورہ فاتحہ نہیں پڑھی (ب) آپ نے فرمایا امام ضامن ہے اور موذن امانت دار ہے
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part One. Book of Prayer. [224 (54)] And whoever intends to enter into the prayer of another needs two intentions: the intention of the prayer and the intention of the imam. From this hadith it is understood that when the imam has recited Fatiha, it is as if the muqtadi has also recited it; he does not remain without Fatiha. (5) From Abu Darda that he heard the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) being asked: 'Is there recitation in every prayer?' He said: 'Yes.' A man from the Ansar said: 'Is this obligatory?' Then he turned to me – and I was the closest of the people to him – and said: 'I think that when the imam leads the people, his recitation suffices them.' (a) (Nasa'i Sharif, Bab Iktifa' al-Ma'mum bi Qira'at al-Imam, p. 07, no. 924; Dar Qutni, p. 326, no. 1248). From this it is also understood that the imam's recitation is sufficient for the muqtadis. (6) In Muwatta of Imam Malik: 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar would not recite behind the imam' (b) (Muwatta Imam Malik, Bab Tark al-Qira'a Khalf al-Imam Fima Jahar, p. 68). (7) If the muqtadi joins the imam in ruku' and thus that rak'ah is obtained for him, but he had no opportunity to recite Fatiha, then according to Imam Shafi'i also in this case the imam's Fatiha suffices for the muqtadi. So in one case he agrees with the Hanafis. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik state that one should recite Fatiha behind the imam, whether the recitation is loud or silent. And there is a narration that if the recitation is silent, one should recite Fatiha, but if loud, one should not. Their proof is the hadith from 'Ubada ibn al-Samit that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'There is no prayer for one who does not recite the Fatiha of the Book' (c) (Bukhari Sharif, Bab Wujub al-Qira'a li-l-Imam wa-l-Ma'mum, p. 104, no. 756; Muslim Sharif, Bab Wujub Qira'at al-Fatiha fi Kull Rak'ah, p. 169, no. 394; Abu Dawud Sharif, no. 823). They prove from this hadith that the muqtadi must also recite Fatiha. Response: The Hanafis also consider Fatiha wajib, but the imam has recited it on behalf of the muqtadi, so it suffices for the muqtadi, as proven by the previous hadiths. It is narrated from Imam Muhammad that based on hadiths, in silent prayer one should recite Fatiha out of precaution (Hidaya, First Chapter on Recitation, p. 101). [224] (54) Whoever intends to enter into another's prayer needs two intentions: the intention of the prayer and the intention of following. When a person follows another, he must make two types of intention: first, the intention of performing the original prayer, and second, the intention of following the imam. (1) Because the imam is the guarantor (dhamin) of the muqtadi's prayer in terms of validity and invalidity. Therefore, he must also intend to follow him. If he does not intend to follow and stands in the row intending only the original prayer, then following does not occur. (2) From Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'The imam is a guarantor (dhamin) and the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy.' (w) (Tirmidhi Sharif, Bab Ma Ja'a anna al-Imam Dhamin wa-l-Mu'adhdhin Mu'taman, p. 51, no. 207). From this it is understood. Footnote: (a) He was asked: 'Is there recitation in every prayer?' He said: 'Yes.' A man from the Ansar said: 'This recitation has become obligatory.' Then the Prophet turned to me – and I was the closest of the people to him – and said: 'I do not think but that when the imam leads the people, his recitation suffices them.' (b) 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar would not recite behind the imam. (c) He said: 'There is no prayer for one who does not recite Surah Fatiha.' (b) He said: 'The imam is a guarantor and the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy.'
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri is a commentary on the ruling for a muqtadi (follower) in congregational prayer. It begins by stating the ruling from the matn: a person entering into another's prayer (i.e., following an imam) needs two intentions – one for the prayer itself and one for following the imam. The commentator then expands on this, connecting it to the debate about reciting Fatiha behind the imam. He presents hadith evidence that the imam's recitation suffices for the muqtadi, citing the hadith of Abu Darda where the Prophet said the imam's recitation is sufficient, and the practice of Ibn 'Umar who did not recite behind the imam. This is the Hanafi position. Then he presents the Shafi'i/Maliki view that the muqtadi must recite Fatiha in every prayer, citing the hadith of 'Ubada. The Hanafi response is that Fatiha is wajib but the imam's recitation fulfills it for the muqtadi, just as in the case where a muqtadi joins late and misses Fatiha – even Shafi'is agree the imam's recitation suffices. The passage ends by repeating the matn on two intentions and providing the hadith 'al-imam dhamin' as proof that the muqtadi must intend to follow the imam, since the imam is responsible for the prayer's validity.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship; here, the muqtadi must intend both the specific prayer and to follow the imam.
اقتداء (iqtida'): The act of following the imam in prayer; requires intention to follow.
ضامن (dhamin): Guarantor or responsible; the imam is responsible for the validity of the muqtadi's prayer.
فاتحة (Fatiha): The opening chapter of the Quran; its recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The muqtadi must recite Fatiha silently.
B) The muqtadi does not recite Fatiha; the imam's recitation suffices.
C) The muqtadi must recite Fatiha loudly.
D) The muqtadi recites Fatiha only if he joins late.

Key Takeaway
The muqtadi must intend to follow the imam, and the imam's recitation of Fatiha suffices for the follower, a unique Hanafi position supported by hadith and the principle of dhaman.

Congregational Prayer: Sunnah Mu'akkadah in the Hanafi School
Ruling that jama'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer and explain why the hadith about burning houses does not establish obligation.

Core Idea
Jama'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah: leaving it without excuse is a sin, but the prayer remains valid.

This passage addresses the legal status of congregational prayer (jama'ah) in the Hanafi school. While the strong prophetic hadith about burning houses might suggest obligation, the Hanafis interpret it as extreme emphasis, maintaining that jama'ah is a strongly recommended sunnah, not a required fard. Understanding how the school reconciles such severe warnings with non-obligatory status is key to grasping Hanafi legal methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? Congregational prayer (jama'ah). What is its ruling according to the Hanafi school? Sunnah mu'akkadah – a strongly emphasized recommended act, not obligatory.
Contrast with other schools: Shafi'i says fard kifayah, Hanbali says fard 'ayn.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Two hadith are cited: (1) The Prophet's intention to burn houses of those who miss congregation, (2) The hadith that the prayer of one who misses without excuse is not accepted. Identify these as ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof indicates the ruling)
The threat of burning houses seems to indicate obligation. However, the Hanafis argue that the Prophet did not actually carry out the threat, and no explicit command (amr) is given. The threat shows extreme emphasis, not legal obligation. The second hadith about non-acceptance is interpreted as loss of perfect reward, not invalidation.
This is a key interpretative move: strong language does not necessarily mean fard.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Internally, Imam Muhammad reportedly considered it wajib. Externally, Shafi'i and Hanbali schools consider it fard. Understand the basis of their disagreement.
For Hanafis, the absence of a clear command (amr) in the Quran or mutawatir sunnah is decisive.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred position)
The majority of Hanafi scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf) hold it as sunnah mu'akkadah. This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling). The strong hadith is not enough to raise it to wajib or fard.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text

Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part One, p. 161. Book of Prayer. Following [the imam]. [225 (55)] And congregational prayer (jama'ah) is a strongly emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah). [226 (56)] And the most deserving of people to lead the prayer is the most knowledgeable among them. 'Because the imam is the guarantor of the muqtadi's prayer, therefore the muqtadi needs to intend (following) the imam.' (2) From Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'The imam is appointed only to be followed, so do not differ with him.' (a) (Muslim Sharif, Bab I'timam al-Ma'mum bi-l-Imam, p. 76, no. 414). From this hadith also the necessity of intending to follow is understood. [225] (55) Congregational prayer is a strongly emphasized sunnah. Explanation of congregational prayer: (1) From Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'By Him in whose hand my soul is, I have thought to order that firewood be gathered, then order the prayer and have the adhan called for it, then order a man to lead the people, then go to some men and burn their houses upon them. By Him in whose hand my soul is, if one of them knew that he would find a fatty bone or two good sheep, he would certainly attend the 'Isha' prayer.' (b) (Bukhari Sharif, Bab Wujub Salat al-Jama'ah, p. 89, no. 644; Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab al-Tashdid fi Tark al-Salah, p. 88, no. 548). The Prophet intended to burn houses for abandoning congregation, which is proof of its obligation. However, it is sunnah mu'akkadah. (2) From Ibn 'Abbas that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Whoever hears the caller (mu'adhdhin) and nothing prevents him from following him – they said: What is an excuse? He said: Fear or illness – his prayer that he prayed (alone) will not be accepted.' (c) (Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab fi al-Tashdid fi Tark al-Jama'ah, p. 88, no. (55)). From this it is also understood that congregation is sunnah mu'akkadah, because leaving it without an excuse results in the prayer not being accepted.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that congregational prayer (jama'ah) is sunnah mu'akkadah (a strongly emphasized sunnah), not fard (obligatory). The commentator first provides a hadith from Abu Huraira where the Prophet (ﷺ) intended to burn the houses of those who missed congregation – this indicates the extreme importance of jama'ah. However, the commentator clarifies that despite this strong indication, the ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib or fard. He then provides another hadith from Ibn 'Abbas stating that the prayer of one who misses congregation without a valid excuse (fear or illness) is not accepted, again emphasizing its importance while maintaining the sunnah classification. The commentator reconciles the strong language of the hadith with the Hanafi position that jama'ah is not obligatory by noting that the Prophet's threat was to emphasize the great reward and sin of leaving it, but not to establish legal obligation. The key point is that jama'ah is highly recommended but not fard.

Key Terms
جماعة (jama'ah): Congregational prayer performed with an imam; for men, it is a strongly emphasized sunnah.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A recommended act that the Prophet regularly performed and emphasized; leaving it without excuse is disliked and may incur sin, but does not invalidate the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, congregational prayer is a strongly emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), not an obligation; its importance is demonstrated by severe prophetic warnings, but the absence of an explicit command keeps it at the sunnah level.

The Most Deserving to Lead Prayer: Hanafi Criteria
Order of priority for who is most deserving to lead prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of priority for selecting an imam and identify the condition under which a previously appointed imam retains priority.

Core Idea
Knowledge of prayer rules is the primary qualification for an imam; recitation, piety, and age follow only when earlier criteria are equal.

This lesson covers the Hanafi criteria for choosing an imam for congregational prayer. The text presents a clear hierarchy, emphasizing that the imam's role is to ensure the validity of the followers' prayer, so knowledge of the fiqh of salah takes precedence over other qualities. Understanding this order helps ensure that the prayer is led properly and in accordance with the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the four criteria in order
The primary criterion is knowledge of sunnah (ahkam al-salah). If equal, then best recitation (qira'ah). If equal, then most pious (awra'). If equal, then oldest in age. This order is fixed and must be applied sequentially.
Sunnah here means the rules of prayer, not general prophetic practice.
2
Understand the equality condition
Each subsequent criterion is considered only if the previous one is equal among the candidates. For example, if one person is more knowledgeable, he is chosen even if others recite better.
Equality in knowledge means comparable understanding of the fiqh of prayer.
3
Note the exception for a previously appointed imam
If a mosque has a permanent imam already appointed, he retains priority over newcomers even if they are more qualified according to the criteria.
This respects established leadership and avoids confusion.
4
Recognize the hadith support
The Prophet ﷺ said, 'The imam is appointed only to be followed, so do not differ with him.' This underscores the importance of proper selection as the imam's decisions affect the congregation.
The hadith is cited in the footnotes of the text.

[226] (56) The most deserving of people for leading the prayer (imamah) is the one among them who knows the sunnah most. Then, if they are equal (in knowledge of sunnah), then the one among them who has the best recitation. If equal in that, then the most pious. If equal in that, then the older in age. By 'sunnah' is meant the rules of prayer. Therefore, the one among those present who is most knowledgeable of the rules of prayer and its issues should be made imam, provided that he knows enough recitation to make the prayer valid. Then if they are equal in knowledge of issues, then the one with very good recitation should be made imam. If they are also equal in recitation, then the more pious should be made imam. If they are equal in piety, then the older in age has the right to imamah. This applies when an imam has not been previously appointed. But if an imam has been previously appointed, then he has a greater right to lead. Footnote: (a) He said: 'The imam is appointed only to be followed, so do not differ with him.' (b) He said: 'By Him in whose hand my soul is, I have thought to order that firewood be gathered, then order the prayer and have the adhan called, then order a man to lead the people, then go to some men and burn their houses...' (c) He said: 'Whoever hears the caller and nothing prevents him from following, they said: What is the excuse? He said: Fear or illness, then his prayer (alone) will not be accepted.'
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi criteria for selecting an imam for prayer. The primary criterion is knowledge of the sunnah, which here specifically means knowledge of the rules (ahkam) of prayer and related fiqh issues. The imam must also have sufficient recitation ability to make the prayer valid. If multiple people are equal in knowledge, then priority goes to the best reciter (qira'ah). If equal in recitation, then the most pious (awra'). If equal in piety, then the oldest in age. This hierarchy is based on the principle that the imam is responsible for the validity of the followers' prayer, so knowledge is most important. The passage also notes that if a permanent imam is already appointed (e.g., for a mosque), he retains priority over newcomers. The footnotes provide supporting hadiths: the imam should be followed, and the severe warning for missing congregation emphasizes the importance of proper leadership.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): In this context, 'sunnah' refers specifically to the rules and regulations of prayer (ahkam al-salah), not general Prophetic practice.
امامة (imamah): The position of leading the congregational prayer; the one who leads is called imam.
قراءة (qira'ah): Recitation of the Quran; here it means the quality and correctness of recitation, including tajweed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Their age
B) Their piety
C) Their recitation quality
D) Their lineage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi priority for imamah is: knowledge of prayer rules first, then recitation, then piety, then age, with the exception of a previously appointed imam retaining priority.

Congregation (Jama'ah) is Sunnah Muakkadah
Ruling with hadith proofs on the status of jama'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer as sunnah muakkadah and explain why the strong hadith threats do not make it obligatory.

Core Idea
Congregation is a confirmed Sunnah, not an obligation—the Prophet's unexecuted threat proves emphasis, not legal duty.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that praying in congregation (jama'ah) is a confirmed Sunnah (sunnah muakkadah), not an obligation. We will analyze two hadiths that seem to demand attendance under threat of burning houses or non-acceptance of prayer. The Hanafi school resolves the apparent contradiction by interpreting these texts as indicating strong recommendation rather than obligation, consistent with the Prophet's action (or inaction). By the end, you will understand the legal reasoning behind this classification and how it differs from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is attending congregational prayer. The Hanafi ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed Sunnah).
Sunnah muakkadah is between wajib and ghayr muakkadah in emphasis.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: the Prophet's threat to burn houses for missing congregation, and his statement that the prayer of one who misses without excuse is not accepted.
Both hadith are from Sahih Bukhari and Sunan Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The threat shows extreme emphasis but the Prophet never executed it, indicating it is not legally binding (wajib). The non-acceptance hadith shows deficiency in reward, not invalidation of the prayer itself.
Hanafi usul holds that an unexecuted threat (tahdid) does not create obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools, such as the Shafi'i and Hanbali, view these same hadith as proof that jama'ah is fard kifayah or even fard 'ayn.
The difference stems from different usul principles regarding commands and threats.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on a holistic reading: the non-execution of the threat, the existence of excuses (fear/illness), and the principle that a strong recommendation is sufficient to explain the hadith.
This position is the mufta bihi (operative) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۲۵] (۵۵) جماعت سنت مؤکدہ ہے۔
جماعت کا بیان کی
(۱) عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله قال والذي نفسي بيده لقد ههمت ان امر ليحطب يحطب ثم امر بالصلوة فيوذن لها ثم امر رجلا فيؤم الناس ثم اخالف الى رجال فاحرق عليهم بيوتهم والذي نفسي بيده لو يعلم احدهم انه يجد عرقا سمينا او مرما تین حسنتين لشهد العشاء (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب وجوب صلوة الجماعة ص ۸۹ نمبر ۶۴۴ رابوداؤد شریف، باب في التشديد في ترك الصلوۃ ص ۸۸ نمبر ۵۴۸) آپ نے جماعت چھوڑنے پر گھروں کو جلا دینے کا ارادہ فرمایا جو جماعت کے وجوب کی دلیل ہے۔ تاہم وہ سنت مؤکدہ ہے (۲) عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله له من سمع المنادى فلم يمنعه من اتباعه
صلى الله
عذر قالوا وما العذر؟ قال خوف او مرض لم تقبل منه الصلوة التي صلى (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی التشدید فی ترک
الجماعة ص ۸۸ نمبر (۵۵) اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ جماعت سنت مؤکدہ ہے۔ کیونکہ بغیر عذر کے اس کے چھوڑنے سے نماز قبول نہیں ہوگی۔
[225] (55) Congregation is a confirmed Sunnah.
Description of congregation:
(1) From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'By the One in Whose hand is my soul, I intended to order that firewood be gathered, then order the prayer and the adhan be called for it, then order a man to lead the people in prayer, then I would go to men and burn their houses upon them. By the One in Whose hand is my soul, if any of them knew that he would find a fat bone or two good meaty trotters, he would attend the Isha prayer.' (Bukhari, Book of Obligation of Congregational Prayer p.89 no.644 and Abu Dawud, Book of Severity in Abandoning Prayer p.88 no.548) The Prophet intended to burn houses for abandoning congregation, which indicates obligation. Nevertheless, it is a confirmed Sunnah. (2) From Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever hears the caller (to prayer) and nothing prevents him from following him - they said: What is the excuse? He said: Fear or illness - his prayer which he prayed is not accepted.' (Abu Dawud, Book of Severity in Abandoning Congregation p.88 no. [55]) From this too it is known that congregation is a confirmed Sunnah, because abandoning it without excuse results in the prayer not being accepted.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It presents the Hanafi position that performing congregational prayer is a confirmed Sunnah (sunnah muakkadah), not obligatory. Two hadith are provided as evidence. The first hadith shows the extreme emphasis: the Prophet threatened to burn the houses of those who miss the congregation, but since he did not actually carry out the threat, it indicates strong recommendation rather than obligation. The second hadith states that the prayer of someone who misses congregation without a valid excuse (fear or illness) is not accepted, meaning it is valid but deficient in reward. The Hanafi school reconciles these proofs by ruling that congregation is sunnah muakkadah – a strongly recommended act that should not be abandoned without excuse, but it is not fard or wajib.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregational prayer performed by two or more persons led by an imam.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah muakkadah): A confirmed Sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and recommended. It is less than wajib but abandoning it without excuse is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal ruling of congregational prayer (jama'ah)?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah muakkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, congregational prayer is sunnah muakkadah—strongly recommended but not obligatory; missing it without excuse diminishes the prayer's acceptance but does not invalidate it.

10 min
Who is Most Entitled to Lead the Prayer (Imamah)
Ranking of persons for imamah with hadith proofs and dispute with Abu Yusuf/Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ranking for imamah and evaluate the dispute with Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i regarding whether knowledge of sunnah or recitation takes precedence.

Core Idea
Knowledge of prayer rulings (sunnah) takes precedence over recitation in choosing an imam.

Choosing the right imam for congregational prayer is a practical issue in every Muslim community. The Hanafi school gives a clear ranking based on the Prophet's practice and hadith, placing deep understanding of salah rulings above mere recitation skill. This lesson unpacks that ranking, the proofs behind it, and the differing opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the four tiers of the ranking: a'lamuhum bi al-sunnah (most knowledgeable of prayer rulings), then aqra'uhum (best reciter), then awra'uhum (most pious), then asannahum (oldest in age).
Note that 'sunnah' here means fiqh al-salah, not the general sunnah.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam Abu Yusuf (from within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that the best reciter takes precedence over the most knowledgeable of sunnah. Recognize their key proof: the hadith of Abu Mas'ud.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith of Abu Mas'ud: 'The one who leads the people should be the one with the most recitation...' and consider how it appears to support the opposite ranking.
Other hadith like 'if equal in Hijrah, the eldest leads' also used.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that during the Prophet's time, good reciters were also knowledgeable of rulings, so the hadith is contextual. They offer counter-proofs: the hadith of Abu Bakr being chosen over Ubayy, and the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud prioritizing understanding.
The Hanafi position is that knowledge of sunnah is more critical for handling issues like sajdah al-sahw and distinguishing fard, wajib, and sunnah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if a person with excellent recitation but limited fiqh knowledge is present, and another with deep fiqh knowledge but average recitation, the Hanafi school says the latter should lead. Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i say the former should lead.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the majority view: knowledge of sunnah first.

(۱) مسئلہ زیادہ جاننے والے کو سب سے مقدم اس لئے کریں گے کہ اس کی ضرورت زیادہ پڑتی ہے کہ کہاں سجدہ سہو ہوگا اور کہاں نہیں ہو گا۔ اسی طرح کون سارکن فرض ہے کون سا واجب اور کون سا سنت ، اور اس کی رعایت کتنی کرنی چاہئے (۲) یوں بھی زیادہ جاننے والے کا رعب زیادہ پڑتا ہے۔ اور اس کی وجہ سے جماعت کا معاملہ قابو میں رہتا ہے (۳) دور صحابہ میں اونچے قاری ابی بن کعب تھے لیکن آپ نے آخر وقت میں اپنے مصلے پر حضرت ابو بکر کو تاکید کر کے کھڑا کیا جو اعلم بالسنتہ تھے ۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اعلم بالسنتہ کو امامت کا حق زیادہ ہے۔ عن ابى موسى قال مرض النبي الله فاشتد مرضة فقال مروا ابا بكر فليصل بالناس (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب اہل العلم و الفضل احق بالا مامته ص ۹۳ نمبر ۶۷۸ ر مسلم شریف ، باب استخلاف الامام اذا عرض له عذرص ۷۸ انمبر ۴۱۸) (۴) عن ابن مسعود قال قال رسول الله الله الله ليلني منكم اولوا الاحلام والنهى ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب تسوية الصفوف واقامتها فضل الاول فالاول ص ۱۸۱ نمبر ۴۳۲ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عقل اور سمجھ رکھنے والے کو امام کے قریب رہنا چاہئے تا کہ ضرورت پر امامت کے کام آئے ۔ یہ نہیں کہا کہ قاری کو حضور کے قریب ہونا چاہئے (۵) حدیث میں ہے عن عقبة بن عمرو قال قال رسول الله له يوم الناس اقدمهم هجرة وان كانوا في الهجرة سواء فافقههم فى الدين وان كانوا في الدين سواء
صلى الله
فاقرؤهم للقرآن ( ج ) ( دار قطنی ، باب من احق بالا مامتہ ص ۲۸۴ نمبر ۱۰۷۲) اس میں بھی افقہ کو زیادہ حق امامت دیا گیا ہے۔ ان امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کی رائے ہے کہ جو اچھا قاری ہو ان کو امامت کا زیادہ حق ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابی مسعود الانصاري قال قال رسول الله الا الله يوم القوم اقرؤهم لكتاب الله فان كانوا فى القراءة سواء فاعلمهم بالسنة فان كانوا في السنة سواء فاقدمهم هجرة . وفي حديث آخر فان كانوا في الهجرة سواء فليؤمهم اكبرهم سنا (و)(مسلم شریف ، باب من احق بالا ملامته ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۶۷۳ را بود اؤ د شریف، باب من احق بالا مامته ص ۹۴ نمبر (۵۸۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو زیادہ قاری ہو وہ امامت کا زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ حضور کے دور میں جو زیادہ قرآن پڑھنے والا ہوتا تھا وہ مسائل کو بھی زیادہ جاننے والا ہوتا تھا اس لئے اقرء بالقرآن فرمایا۔ زیادہ عمر والے کو امامت کا حق ہوگا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن مالک بن الحویرث قال قدمنا على النبي ... قال ... فاذا حضرت الصلوة فليؤذن لكم احدكم وليؤمكم اکبر کم (ه) بخاری شریف، باب اذا استود في القراءة فليو ته اکبر هم ص ۹۴ نمبر ۶۸۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سبھی ہجرت اور قرآت میں برابر ہوں تو عمر کے اعتبار سے جو حاشیہ : (الف) حضور بیمار ہوئے پھر ان کا مرض بڑھ گیا تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ ابو بکر کوحکم دو کہ وہ لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائے (ب ) آپ نے فرمایا میرے قریب تمہارے بالغ اور عقل والے رہا کریں۔ پھر جو ان سے کم درجہ کے ہوں، پھر جو ان سے کم درجہ کے ہوں (ج) آپ نے فرمایا لوگوں کی امامت وہ کریں جو ان میں سے ہجرت کے اعتبار سے قدیم ہوں۔ اور اگر ہجرت میں برابر ہوں تو دین کے انتہار سے جو زیادہ فقیہ ہوں۔ اور اگر دین میں برابر ہوں تو جو قرآن کا زیادہ قاری ہوں ( د ) آپ نے فرمایا قوم کی امامت وہ کریں جو اللہ کی کتاب کو زیادہ پڑھنے والا ہو ۔ پس اگر وہ قرآت میں برابر ہوں تو جو ان میں سے سنت کو زیادہ جاننے والا ہو ۔ پس اگر سنت میں برابر ہوں تو جو ان میں سے ہجرت کے اعتبار سے قدیم ہو۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے جو ہجرت کے اعتبار سے برابر ہوں تو ان کی امامت کرے جو عمر کے اعتبار سے بڑا ہو (ہ) آپ نے فرمایا جب نماز کا وقت آئے تو تمہارے لئے کوئی اذان دے اور تم میں سے بڑا تمہاری امامت کرے۔
[226] (56) The most entitled person among people to lead the prayer is the one among them who knows the Sunnah most. Then, if they are equal (in knowledge of Sunnah), then the one with the best recitation among them; if they are equal in that, then the most pious; and if they are equal in that, then the one who is older in age.
By 'Sunnah' is meant the rulings of prayer. Therefore, among those present, the one who is most acquainted with the rulings of prayer and issues should be made imam, provided he knows enough recitation to make the prayer valid. Then, if all are equal in knowledge of issues, the one whose recitation is excellent should be made imam. And if all are equal in recitation, then the one who is more pious should be made imam. And if all are equal in piety, then the one older in age has the right to be imam.
This applies when no imam has been previously appointed. But if an imam has been previously appointed, then he has more right to lead.
Footnote: (a) He (peace be upon him) said: The imam is only appointed to be followed, so do not differ with him. (b) He said... (c) He said...
By the Sunnah, so if they are equal, then the best reciter; if equal, then the most pious; if equal, then the eldest. (1) The reason the one with more knowledge is given precedence is because his need is greater: where should the prostration of forgetfulness be performed and where not. Similarly, which pillar is obligatory, which is wajib, and which is sunnah, and how much consideration should be given. (2) Also, the one with more knowledge commands more respect, and through this the congregation remains under control. (3) During the time of the Companions, Ubayy bin Ka'b was a great reciter, but the Prophet at the end of his life insisted on having Abu Bakr stand on his prayer mat, who was more knowledgeable of the Sunnah. This shows that the one most knowledgeable of the Sunnah has more right to lead. From Abu Musa: The Prophet fell ill and his illness became severe, so he said: 'Tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer.' (Bukhari and Muslim) (4) From Ibn Mas'ud: The Prophet said: 'Let those among you who are mature and wise stand near me, then those next to them, then those next to them.' (Muslim) This hadith indicates that the intelligent and wise should stand near the imam so that they can take over the imamah when needed. It does not say that the reciter should be near him. (5) There is a hadith from Uqbah bin Amr: The Prophet said: 'The one who leads the people should be the one with the earliest Hijrah; if they are equal in Hijrah, then the one most learned in religion; if they are equal in religion, then the one with the most recitation of the Quran.' (Dar Qutni) This also gives more right to the faqih. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i are of the opinion that the one who is a good reciter has more right to lead. Their evidence is the hadith of Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari: The Prophet said: 'The one who leads the people should be the one with the most recitation of the Book of Allah; if they are equal in recitation, then the one most knowledgeable of the Sunnah; if they are equal in the Sunnah, then the one with the earliest Hijrah.' And in another hadith: 'If they are equal in Hijrah, then the eldest among them should lead.' (Muslim and Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that the one with more recitation is more entitled to lead. We say: During the Prophet's time, those who recited more were also more knowledgeable of the rulings, so he said 'let the one with more recitation' lead. The one with more age has the right to lead; evidence for this is the hadith of Malik bin al-Huwayrith: 'When the time for prayer comes, let one of you call the adhan and let the eldest among you lead you.' (Bukhari) This hadith shows that when all are equal in Hijrah and recitation, then the one older in age should lead. Footnote: (a) The Prophet fell ill... (b) He said... (c) He said... (d) He said... (e) He said: When the time for prayer comes, let one of you call the adhan and let the eldest among you lead you.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This is a ruling with proofs and an inter-madhhab dispute. The passage establishes the Hanafi ranking for who is most entitled to be the imam in congregational prayer. The priority is: 1) the one with the most knowledge of the rulings of prayer (sunnah), 2) then the one with the best recitation (qira'ah), 3) then the most pious (awra'), 4) then the eldest in age (asann). The author explains that 'sunnah' here means the fiqh of prayer – knowledge of conditions, pillars, wajibat, etc. The need for such knowledge is greater because the imam must handle issues like sajdah al-sahw and know the difference between fard, wajib, and sunnah. The text supports this with several hadith: the Prophet choosing Abu Bakr (most knowledgeable of sunnah) over Ubayy (great reciter); the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud emphasizing maturity and understanding; and the hadith of Uqbah bin Amr prioritizing fiqh over qira'ah. The passage then addresses the opposing view of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i, who prioritize qira'ah based on the hadith of Abu Mas'ud that mentions recitation first. The Hanafi response is that during the Prophet's time, those with excellent recitation were also knowledgeable of rulings, so the hadith is contextual. The final ruling (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the majority position: knowledge of sunnah comes first.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): In this context, 'sunnah' refers to the detailed rulings of prayer (ahkam al-salah), including the conditions, pillars, wajibat, sunan, and related issues.
الإمامة (al-imamah): The position of leading the congregational prayer.
القراءة (al-qira'ah): Recitation of the Quran during prayer; correctness and beauty are considered here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (majority), who should be given priority as imam in a congregation?
A) The one with the best recitation
B) The one with the most knowledge of the rulings of prayer (sunnah)
C) The one who is oldest in age
D) The one with the loudest voice

Key Takeaway
The most entitled to lead prayer is the one with the most knowledge of prayer rulings (sunnah), followed by recitation, piety, and age.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Imamate Priority: Knowledge vs. Recitation
Inter-madhhab dispute on imamate priority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on imamate priority, identify the opposing evidence, and apply the Hanafi rebuttal to a congregational scenario.

Core Idea
Knowledge of fiqh, not recitation skill, determines imamate priority in the Hanafi school.

When a congregation has both a scholar and a skilled reciter, who should lead? This passage presents the Hanafi argument that the most knowledgeable in Sunnah (fiqh) is preferred, citing the Prophet's appointment of Abu Bakr and other hadith. You will learn to navigate the textual evidence and understand the practical implications of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Claim
Find the author's statement: the most knowledgeable in Sunnah is given priority over the best reciter. Note the three reasons given: practical need, awe, and historical precedent.
The author uses 'اعلم بالسنتہ' as the key criterion.
2
Extract the Hanafi Proof Texts
List the hadith cited for the Hanafi position: Abu Bakr's appointment (Bukhari/Muslim), Ibn Mas'ud (about wise companions), and Uqbah ibn 'Amr (prioritizing fiqh). Understand how each supports knowledge over recitation.
Note that the Uqbah hadith explicitly puts fiqh before recitation.
3
Understand the Opposing View
Identify that Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i uphold recitation priority, citing the hadith from Abu Mas'ud that begins with 'أقرؤهم لكتاب الله'.
The opposition claims the wording 'أقرؤهم' is the primary criterion.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
Read how the author rebuts: arguing that in the Prophet's era, good reciters were also knowledgeable, so 'أقرؤهم' implied comprehensive knowledge. Also, the Malik ibn al-Huwayrith hadith uses age as a tiebreaker, not raising recitation above knowledge.
The response refutes the apparent plain meaning of the hadith.
5
Determine the Practical Result (Thamarah)
Conclude that if both a scholar and a better reciter are present, the Hanafi ruling is to choose the scholar. The opposite ruling would choose the reciter.
This ikhtilaf has real consequences for congregational prayer.

زیادہ حق ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابی مسعود الانصاري قال قال رسول الله الا الله يوم القوم اقرؤهم لكتاب الله فان كانوا فى القراءة سواء فاعلمهم بالسنة فان كانوا في السنة سواء فاقدمهم هجرة . وفي حديث آخر فان كانوا في الهجرة سواء فليؤمهم اكبرهم سنا (و)(مسلم شریف ، باب من احق بالا ملامته ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۶۷۳ را بود اؤ د شریف، باب من احق بالا مامته ص ۹۴ نمبر (۵۸۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو زیادہ قاری ہو کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن مالک بن الحویرث قال قدمنا على النبي ... قال ... فاذا حضرت الصلوة فليؤذن لكم احدكم وليؤمكم اکبر کم (ه) بخاری شریف، باب اذا استود في القراءة فليو ته اکبر هم ص ۹۴ نمبر ۶۸۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سبھی ہجرت اور قرآت میں برابر ہوں تو عمر کے اعتبار سے جو حاشیہ : (الف) حضور بیمار ہوئے پھر ان کا مرض بڑھ گیا تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ ابو بکر کوحکم دو کہ وہ لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائے (ب ) آپ نے فرمایا میرے قریب تمہارے بالغ اور عقل والے رہا کریں۔ پھر جو ان سے کم درجہ کے ہوں، پھر جو ان سے کم درجہ کے ہوں (ج) آپ نے فرمایا لوگوں کی امامت وہ کریں جو ان میں سے ہجرت کے اعتبار سے قدیم ہوں۔ اور اگر ہجرت میں برابر ہوں تو دین کے انتہار سے جو زیادہ فقیہ ہوں۔ اور اگر دین میں برابر ہوں تو جو قرآن کا زیادہ قاری ہوں ( د ) آپ نے فرمایا قوم کی امامت وہ کریں جو اللہ کی کتاب کو زیادہ پڑھنے والا ہو ۔ پس اگر وہ قرآت میں برابر ہوں تو جو ان میں سے سنت کو زیادہ جاننے والا ہو ۔ پس اگر سنت میں برابر ہوں تو جو ان میں سے ہجرت کے اعتبار سے قدیم ہو۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے جو ہجرت کے اعتبار سے برابر ہوں تو ان کی امامت کرے جو عمر کے اعتبار سے بڑا ہو (ہ) آپ نے فرمایا جب نماز کا وقت آئے تو تمہارے لئے کوئی اذان دے اور تم میں سے بڑا تمہاری امامت کرے۔
Question: The one with more knowledge will be given priority because his need is greater: he knows where the prostration of forgetfulness occurs and where it does not. Similarly, which pillar is fard, which is wajib, and which is sunnah, and how much care is needed. (2) Also, the one with more knowledge has more awe, and thereby the affair of the congregation remains under control. (3) In the era of the Companions, there was the great reciter Ubayy ibn Ka'b, but at the end of his life the Prophet insisted on Abu Bakr to lead, who was the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah. This shows that the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah has more right to imamate. From Abu Musa: the Prophet fell ill, and his illness became severe, so he said: 'Tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer.' (a) (Bukhari, chapter on people of knowledge and virtue being more entitled to imamate, p. 93 no. 678; Muslim, chapter on appointing a deputy when an excuse arises, p. 78 no. 418) (4) From Ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet said: 'Let those among you who are mature and sensible be near me, then those next to them, then those next to them.' (b) (Muslim, chapter on straightening the rows and establishing their virtue, p. 181 no. 432) This hadith shows that the intelligent should be near the imam so that in need they can serve as imam. It does not say that the reciter should be near the Prophet. (5) There is a hadith from Uqbah ibn Amr: the Prophet said: 'The people's imam should be the foremost in hijrah; if they are equal in hijrah, then the most jurist in religion; if they are equal in religion, then the most reciter of the Quran.' (c) (Darqutni, chapter on who is most entitled to imamate, p. 284 no. 1072) In this also, the most jurist is given more right to imamate. Now, Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold that the good reciter has more right to imamate. Their evidence is the hadith from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari: the Prophet said: 'The leader of the people should be the most reciter of the Book of Allah; if they are equal in recitation, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah; if they are equal in the Sunnah, then the foremost in hijrah.' And in another hadith: 'If they are equal in hijrah, then let the eldest lead them.' (d) (Muslim, chapter on who is most entitled to imamate, p. 236 no. 673; Abu Dawud, chapter on who is most entitled to imamate, p. 94 no. 582) This hadith shows that the better reciter is more entitled to imamate. We say that in the Prophet's time, whoever was a better reciter was also more knowledgeable of issues; therefore, he said 'the most reciter of the Quran.' The older one will have the right to imamate; the evidence is the hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: we came to the Prophet... he said: 'When prayer time comes, let one of you give the adhan and let the eldest among you lead you.' (h) (Bukhari, chapter on if they are equal in recitation, let the eldest lead, p. 94 no. 685) This hadith shows that if all are equal in hijrah and recitation, then the eldest leads. Footnotes: (a) The Prophet fell ill, then his illness worsened, so he said: order Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer. (b) He said: let the mature and sensible among you remain near me, then those below them, then those below them. (c) He said: the people's imam should be the foremost in hijrah; if they are equal in hijrah, then the most jurist in religion; if they are equal in religion, then the most reciter of the Quran. (d) He said: the leader of the people should be the most reciter of the Book of Allah; then if they are equal in recitation, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah; then if they are equal in the Sunnah, then the foremost in hijrah. In another hadith: if they are equal in hijrah, then let the eldest lead them. (h) He said: when prayer time comes, let one of you give the adhan and let the eldest among you lead you.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the primary qualification for imamate (leading prayer). The Hanafi position, attributed to Abu Hanifa, is that the most knowledgeable in the Sunnah (fiqh) is preferred over the best reciter. The author presents three reasons: (1) practical need: the imam must know rulings like sajdah al-sahw and the difference between fard, wajib, and sunnah; (2) psychological: knowledge commands respect and control over the congregation; (3) historical: the Prophet appointed Abu Bakr, who was knowledgeable in Sunnah, over Ubayy ibn Ka'b, who was a great reciter. Then he cites hadith from Abu Musa (about Abu Bakr) and Ibn Mas'ud (about proximity of wise companions) to support knowledge priority. Another hadith (from Uqbah) explicitly prioritizes fiqh over recitation. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i argue from a hadith (Abu Mas'ud) that prioritizes recitation first. The Hanafi response: in the Prophet's era, reciters were also jurists, so 'aqra' (most reciter) implied knowledge; the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith shows age as a tiebreaker when recitation and hijrah are equal. The Hanafi school thus maintains that knowledge (fiqh) is the primary criterion, and recitation is secondary.

Key Terms
اعلم بالسنتہ (a'lam bis-sunnah): The most knowledgeable in the prophetic traditions and the derivations of rulings (fiqh).
اقرؤهم (aqra'uhum): The one who recites the Quran most accurately and with proper tajweed.
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness to compensate for an omission or addition in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, who should be given priority to lead the prayer?
A) The one with the most beautiful voice in recitation
B) The one who is most knowledgeable in the Sunnah (fiqh)
C) The one who is oldest in age
D) The one who migrated first

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the most knowledgeable in fiqh (a'lam bis-sunnah) is given precedence over the best reciter for leading prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Imamate of Certain Individuals: Makruh but Valid
Ruling with proofs on imamate of disliked individuals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imamate of a slave, bedouin, fasiq, blind, and illegitimate child, and explain why it is makruh but valid.

Core Idea
Appointing a disliked imam is makruh, but the prayer remains valid — karahah does not nullify obligation.

In this passage, the author addresses a common concern: who can lead the prayer? Some individuals are considered less suitable due to social status or personal qualities. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling: the imamate of such persons is disliked (makruh) but their prayer is valid. This lesson unpacks the evidence and conditions that remove the dislike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the individuals mentioned
The passage lists five types: a slave, a bedouin (rustic), a fasiq (sinner), a blind person, and an illegitimate child (walad al-zina).
These categories share a common feature: they are typically looked down upon in society.
2
State the ruling for each
The ruling is identical for all: it is makruh (disliked) to appoint them as imam, but if they are appointed, the prayer is valid (ja'iz).
The karahah here is tanzihiyyah (light dislike), not tahrimi (prohibitive).
3
Understand the reason for karahah
The primary reason is that these individuals generally lack knowledge ('have ignorance') and the congregation dislikes their imamate. For the blind, an additional reason is the inability to avoid impurity (najasa).
The hadith 'Allah does not accept the prayer of one who leads a people who dislike him' supports the karahah.
4
Note the exceptions
If the individual is knowledgeable and the congregation is pleased with his imamate, the karahah lifts. For the blind, if he can avoid impurity, it is not makruh.
These exceptions show the ruling is conditional, not absolute.
5
Analyze the proofs
The author cites multiple proofs: the hadith of Ibn Umar about dislike, the incident of Aisha led by her slave Zakwan (validity), the statement of Uthman about praying behind a fasiq, the hadith 'pray behind every righteous and sinful person', and the Prophet's appointment of the blind Ibn Umm Maktum as imam.
These evidences establish both the validity and the dislike.

227 (57) It is makruh to put forward a slave, a bedouin, a fasiq, a blind person, and an illegitimate child as imam; if they are put forward, it is permissible. It is makruh to appoint a slave, bedouin, fasiq, blind, and illegitimate child as imam. If they are appointed, it is valid. (1) These people generally have ignorance, and the congregation dislike their imamate. Therefore, their imamate is makruh. But if they have knowledge and the congregation are pleased with their imamate, then their imamate is not makruh. For the blind, there is also the reason that he cannot avoid impurity. If he can avoid impurity, it will not be makruh. (2) The hadith: from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet used to say: 'Allah does not accept the prayer of three: one who leads a people who dislike him.' (a) (Abu Dawud, chapter on the man who leads a people who dislike him, p. 95 no. 593) This hadith shows that the imamate of those whom the congregation dislike is makruh. And since people generally dislike the imamate of the above-mentioned individuals, their imamate is makruh. Nevertheless, the imamate will be valid. The evidence for the validity of a slave's imamate is the athar: 'Aisha was led by her slave Zakwan from the Quran.' (b) (Bukhari, chapter on imamate of a slave and client, p. 96 no. 692) The imamate of a fasiq is permissible but makruh; the evidence is the hadith from Ubaydullah ibn Adi ibn al-Khiyar that he entered upon Uthman ibn Affan while he was besieged, and said: 'You are the general imam, and this situation has befallen you, and an imam of fitna leads us and we feel uncomfortable.' He said: 'Prayer is the best thing people do; so if people do good, do good with them; if they do evil, avoid their evil.' (c) (Bukhari, chapter on imamate of the plagued and innovator, p. 96 no. 695) This athar shows that prayer behind a fasiq is permissible, though makruh. And al-Zuhri said: 'We do not consider it good to pray behind an effeminate except in unavoidable necessity.' (d) (Bukhari, same chapter) This also shows that in necessity, prayer behind a fasiq is permissible. From Abu Huraira: the Prophet said: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person, and pray over every righteous and sinful person.' (Sunan al-Sa'id? [؟], chapter on prayer over one who killed himself without considering it legal, fourth, book of funerals, p. 29 no. 6832) Regarding the blind: the hadith from Anas that the Prophet appointed Ibn Umm Maktum as deputy in Medina to lead the people while he was blind. (h) (Abu Dawud, chapter... Footnotes: (a) He said: Allah does not accept the prayer of three: one who leads a people while they dislike him. (b) Aisha was led by her slave Zakwan from the Quran. (c) Ubaydullah ibn Adi entered upon Uthman ibn Affan while he was besieged... (d) Imam al-Zuhri said: I do not consider it good to pray behind an effeminate except in necessity. (h) The Prophet appointed Abdullah ibn Umm Maktum as his deputy in Medina; he used to lead the people while he was blind.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proofs. The author states that it is makruh (disliked) to put forward a slave, bedouin, fasiq (sinner), blind person, or illegitimate child as imam, but if they do lead, the prayer is valid (ja'iz). The reasoning: these individuals generally lack knowledge, and the congregation dislikes their imamate. However, if they are knowledgeable and the congregation is pleased, the karahah disappears. For the blind, an additional reason is inability to avoid impurity. The evidence includes: hadith about one who leads people who dislike him (prayer not accepted), which implies karahah; athar that Aisha was led by her slave Zakwan (showing validity); the incident with Uthman where he implied prayer behind a fasiq is permissible despite dislike; hadith to pray behind every righteous and sinful person; and the Prophet's appointment of the blind Ibn Umm Maktum as imam. The karahah is thus tanzihiyyah (slight dislike), not tahrimi (prohibitive), because the prayer is valid.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): An action that is disliked but not sinful; avoiding it is rewarded but doing it is not punished.
جائز (ja'iz): Permissible and valid in the sense that the prayer fulfills the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason the imamate of a bedouin is makruh?
A) Because bedouins are not trustworthy.
B) Because they generally have ignorance and the congregation dislikes them.
C) Because they cannot recite Quran properly.
D) Because they are impure.

Key Takeaway
The imamate of a slave, bedouin, fasiq, blind, and illegitimate child is makruh but valid; the karahah is conditional on ignorance and congregational dislike.

Five Types of Disliked Imams in Congregational Prayer
Lists five disliked imams with proofs from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five types of people whose imamate is disliked (makruh tanzihi) in the Hanafi school, explain the reasons for dislike, and identify the conditions when the dislike vanishes.

Core Idea
Prayer behind a slave, Bedouin, fasiq, blind person, or illegitimate child is valid but disliked unless knowledge and congregation's pleasure remove the dislike.

The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance on who should lead congregational prayer. This passage addresses five categories of individuals whose imamate is considered makruh tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited) due to common ignorance or public aversion. However, if the imam possesses religious knowledge and the congregation is content, the dislike disappears. We will examine the ruling, its conditions, and the hadith proofs that establish it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five types and the ruling
Read the list of five individuals: a slave, a Bedouin, a fasiq (open sinner), a blind person, and an illegitimate child (walad al-zina). Note that the ruling is 'makruh' (disliked) but the prayer is valid (jā'iz).
The base ruling is makruh tanzihi, not haram.
2
Understand the reasons for dislike
The text gives two primary reasons: common ignorance among these types (lack of knowledge of prayer rulings) and the congregation's dislike of their leadership. For the blind, an additional reason is inability to detect impurity.
Dislike is tied to the congregation's sentiment and the imam's knowledge.
3
Learn when dislike vanishes
If the imam has knowledge (e.g., a learned slave or blind person) and the congregation is pleased, the dislike is removed. For the blind, if he can avoid impurity (e.g., has a helper or can check himself), dislike also disappears.
Knowledge and public acceptance override the general ruling.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
The passage cites multiple proofs: a hadith about three whose prayer is not accepted (Abu Dawud), Aisha's slave leading her (Bukhari), the permissibility of praying behind a fasiq (hadith from Uthman and Abu Hurairah), and the Prophet's appointment of a blind imam (Abu Dawud).
Each proof addresses a specific type or the general principle.
5
Summarize the legal outcome
Synthesize: the imamate of these five is valid (the prayer counts), but it is disliked and should be avoided unless conditions are met. The evidence supports both validity and dislike.
This is a clear example of makruh tanzih—reward is diminished but the act is sound.

227 (57) It is disliked to put forward a slave, a Bedouin, a sinful person, a blind person, and an illegitimate child (to lead prayer). If they do lead, it is permissible. The more pious one has more right to leadership. (227) (57) It is disliked to put forward a slave for imamate, and a Bedouin, a sinful person, a blind person, and an illegitimate child. So if they are put forward, it is permissible. (1) Among these people, ignorance is common, and people dislike their leadership. Therefore their leadership is disliked. But if these people have knowledge and the congregation is pleased with their leadership, then their leadership is not disliked. For the blind, one reason is that he cannot avoid impurity. If he can avoid impurity, it is not disliked. (2) Hadith: From Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to say: 'Three persons whose prayer Allah does not accept: a man who leads a people while they dislike him...' (Abu Dawud). This hadith shows that leadership of people whom the congregation dislikes is disliked. And the congregation dislikes the leadership of the above-mentioned people, therefore their leadership is disliked. Nevertheless, the prayer is valid. Evidence for permissibility of a slave leading: The effect that Aisha was led by her slave Zakwan from the Quran (Bukhari). The leadership of a sinful person is permissible but disliked; evidence: Hadith of Ubaidullah ibn Adi that he entered upon Uthman ibn Affan while besieged... (Bukhari). This effect shows that prayer behind a sinful person can be offered, although it is disliked. Al-Zuhri said: 'We do not think that prayer should be offered behind an effeminate person except out of necessity.' (Bukhari). This also shows that when necessary, prayer behind a sinful person can be offered. From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person, and pray over every righteous and sinful person.' (Sunan). Regarding the blind imam, hadith: From Anas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) appointed Ibn Umm Maktum to lead the people while he was blind (Abu Dawud). Footnotes: (a) He said: Allah does not accept the prayer of three people: a man who leads a people while they dislike him... (b) Aisha was led by her slave Zakwan reciting from the Quran. (c) Ubaidullah ibn Adi entered upon Uthman while he was besieged... (d) Imam Zuhri said: I do not consider it good to pray behind an effeminate person except out of necessity. (e) The Prophet made Abdullah ibn Maktum the caliph over Medina; he led the people while blind. Concluded: It is permissible.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning individuals whose imamate (leadership in prayer) is disliked (makruh) but valid. The text lists five types: a slave, a Bedouin, a sinful person (fasiq), a blind person, and an illegitimate child (walad al-zina). The ruling is from the Hanafi school: it is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited) to appoint such persons as imam, primarily because they are often ignorant of prayer rulings or because people dislike their leadership. However, if they possess knowledge and the congregation is pleased, the dislike is removed. For the blind, the additional reason is inability to detect impurity. The passage provides hadith proofs: a hadith from Abu Dawud states that prayer is not accepted if the congregation dislikes the imam. For the slave, the practice of Aisha being led by her slave Zakwan is cited (Bukhari). For the fasiq, the hadith of Uthman ibn Affan advising prayer behind an imam of trial is quoted, along with a narration from Abu Hurairah commanding prayer behind every righteous and sinful person. For the blind, the Prophet's appointment of Ibn Umm Maktum as imam is evidence (Abu Dawud). The passage concludes that although disliked, the prayer is valid (jāz).

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked but not prohibited; prayer is valid but less reward.
إمامة (imamah): Leading others in congregational prayer.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins.
ولد الزنا (walad al-zina): Child born out of wedlock (illegitimate).
إعرابي (a'rabi): Bedouin; desert dweller often lacking knowledge of Islamic rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that imamate of a slave, Bedouin, fasiq, blind person, or illegitimate child is valid but disliked, with the dislike removed if the imam has knowledge and the congregation is pleased, and for the blind, if he can avoid impurity.

Imam Should Not Prolong Prayer for the Congregation
Ruling that imam should shorten prayer to avoid hardship; with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on prolonging prayer as an imam and identify the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
An imam who prolongs prayer causes hardship and makes people avoid the congregation, which is disliked (makruh tanzih).

This lesson examines a key principle of congregational prayer: the imam must consider the congregation's capacity. The source text establishes that prolonging prayer beyond the sunnah is disliked because it burdens the weak, elderly, and those with needs. We will explore the hadith evidence and the ruling's implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Prolonging prayer by the imam. The text says 'yanbaghi' (it is befitting) not to prolong, which indicates a strong recommendation. Identify the hukm level: makruh tanzih (disliked).
The term 'yanbaghi' in Hanafi fiqh often denotes a sunnah or mustahabb level, but the context of causing hardship raises it to makruh.
2
Extract the Underlying Cause (Illah)
Why is prolongation disliked? Because it causes hardship (mashaqqah) to the weak, elderly, and those with needs. The hadith explicitly mentions these groups. This illah is the basis for the ruling.
The illah of hardship is consistent with the Hanafi principle of lifting hardship (raf' al-haraj).
3
Analyze the Hadith Proof
The hadith from Bukhari and Muslim reports the Prophet's anger at a man who prolonged prayer, and his command 'Whoever leads the people, let him be brief'. The command ('falyatajawwaz') indicates a directive that yields a disliked ruling when violated. Note also the exception: when praying alone, one may prolong.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear and supported by practice.
4
Distinguish the Ruling for the Imam vs. the Individual
The same hadith contrasts: 'And when one of you prays alone, let him prolong as much as he wishes.' Thus the ruling is context-dependent. The imam must consider the congregation; the individual has full freedom.
This distinction shows that the ruling is not about the act itself but about its effect on others.

[228] (58) It is befitting for the imam not to prolong prayer for them. (59) It is disliked for women... From this it is known that if a blind person is careful about impurity and is respected among the people, he can be made imam; it is not disliked. [228] (58) It is appropriate for the imam not to make the prayer very long for the followers. (1) In making prayer very long, weak and old people will be distressed, which is not permissible. Therefore one should not lengthen the recitation beyond the recommended amount. Yes, if he is praying alone, he can lengthen as much as he wishes. (2) Hadith: Abu Mas'ud reported that a man said: 'By Allah, O Messenger of Allah, I delay the morning prayer because of so-and-so who prolongs it for us.' Whoever leads the people in prayer, let him be brief, for among them are the weak, the elderly, and the one with a need.' (Bukhari, Muslim). In another hadith: 'And when one of you prays alone, let him prolong as much as he wishes.' (Bukhari, Muslim). From this it is learned that if one is an imam, he should not prolong prayer; if alone, he may prolong as much as he wishes.

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the length of congregational prayer. The text states that it is befitting (yanbaghi) for the imam not to prolong the prayer for the congregation. The reason given is that prolonged prayer causes hardship for the weak, elderly, and those with urgent needs, and causing such hardship is not permissible. The ruling applies only when leading others; if one prays alone, he may lengthen as desired. The proof is a hadith from Bukhari and Muslim where the Prophet (peace be upon him) became angry at a person who prolonged the morning prayer, and he instructed imams to be brief, considering the congregation's condition. Another narration confirms that one may prolong when praying alone. This is a established ruling in the Hanafi school: the imam should not exceed the sunnah recitation length.

Key Terms
ينبغي (yanbaghi): It is befitting or recommended; indicates a sunnah or mustahabb level.
يتجوز (yatajawwaz): To be brief, to shorten the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is prohibited to prolong.

Key Takeaway
An imam should avoid prolonging prayer to prevent hardship; the hadith commands brevity when leading others, while allowing length when alone.
