Women Leading Women in Congregational Prayer
Ruling on women's congregation and position of woman imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's congregational prayer and identify the position of the woman imam with its evidence from the practice of Aisha and Umm Salamah.

Core Idea
Women leading women in prayer is permissible but disliked; the imam stands in the middle, not in front.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Hanafi fiqh: the permissibility and dislike (karahah) of women forming their own congregational prayer. While the act is valid, the school considers it makruh tanzihi due to modesty considerations. The key point is the positioning of the woman imam — she stands in the middle of the row, not ahead like a man. This ruling is supported by the practice of Aisha and Umm Salamah, as narrated in Darqutni.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is women praying in congregation without any men present. The ruling: it is makruh (disliked) but valid if performed.
Makruh here is tanzihi, not tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil
What is the proof cited? The text quotes the practice of Aisha and Umm Salamah leading women and standing in the middle.
The hadith is from Darqutni, classified as ahad.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof establish the ruling? The fact that they stood in the middle, not in front, indicates the recommended position. The proof also shows that women leading is permissible.
The Hanafi school uses this as a model for the woman imam's position.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Do other schools differ? Yes, some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not consider women's congregation disliked; they see it as valid without dislike.
This is a valid ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is based on specific reasoning.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which view is relied upon in the school? The mufta bihi is that it is disliked but valid, and the woman imam stands in the middle. No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is mentioned.

ہوگی جیسے ننگے کھڑے ہوتے ہیں۔
نماز لئے ہی کو اور صرف عورتیں نماز پڑھیں تو الگ الگ نماز پڑھیں گے۔ کیونکہ وہاں مرد نہیں ہے اس لئے عورت ہی کو امامت کرنی ہوگی۔ اور عورت کی امامت جائز تو ہے لیکن مکروہ ہے۔ اور جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی اور عورت نے امامت کرائی تو امام عورت عورتوں کے درمیان کھڑی ہوگی۔ مرد کی طرح آگے کھڑی نہیں ہوگی۔
ے اس لئے کہ یہ عورتوں کے ستر کے خلاف ہے۔ اس لئے امام عورت درمیان میں کھڑی ہو گی جیسے تمام ننگے آدمیوں کا امام درمیان میں کھڑا ہوتا ہے (۲) عـن ريـطة الحنفية قالت امتنا عائشة فقامت بينهن في الصلوة المكتوبة في حديث آخر امتنا ام سلمة في صلوة العصر فقامت بيننا (ب) (دار قطنی ، باب صلوۃ النساء جماعة وموقف اما محصن ص ۱۳۸۸ نمبر ۱۴۹۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت امام کو درمیان میں کھڑی ہونی چاہیئے۔
[229] (59) It is disliked for women to pray in congregation among themselves. If they do so, the imam will stand in the middle of them, just as naked men stand. They only pray [in congregation] when there is no man; then a woman must lead. And the imamate of a woman is permissible but disliked. When a woman leads, she stands in the middle of the women, not in front like a man. This is because it violates women's covering. So the woman imam stands in the middle, just as the imam of naked men stands in the middle. (2) From Raitah al-Hanafiyyah: 'Aisha led us and stood between us in the obligatory prayer.' In another hadith: 'Umm Salamah led us in Asr prayer and stood between us.' (Darqutni). This effect shows that the woman imam must stand in the middle.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding women's congregational prayer when only women are present. The text states that it is disliked (makruh) for women to form a congregation among themselves. However, if they do, the woman imam stands in the middle of the row, not in front like a man. The reason given is modesty and covering. The imam's position in the middle is analogous to the case of naked men (where the imam stands in the middle to avoid exposure). The ruling is justified by the practice of Aisha and Umm Salamah, who led women in prayer and stood in the middle. The text clarifies that if no man is present, a woman must lead, but it remains disliked. This is a specific Hanafi ruling: women's congregational prayer is valid but makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked but valid; here refers to women's congregation.
الامام (al-imam): The person leading prayer; for women, stands in middle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where should a woman imam stand when leading women in congregational prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) In front of the first row like a man.
B) In the middle of the row of women.
C) Behind all women.
D) She cannot lead at all.

Key Takeaway
Women leading women in congregational prayer is permissible but makruh tanzih; the imam stands in the middle of the row, as practiced by Aisha and Umm Salamah.

Imam Should Not Lengthen Prayer
Ruling that the imam should shorten prayer for the congregation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam lengthening prayer, identify the primary dalil, and explain the wisdom behind shortening.

Core Idea
The imam must consider the congregation; prolonging prayer is makruh tanzihi, and shortening is recommended.

This lesson addresses the etiquette of the imam leading prayer. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the imam should not lengthen the prayer excessively, as it causes hardship. The evidence comes from the Prophet's ﷺ stern warning against causing aversion. Understanding this ruling ensures the imam maintains the congregation's comfort.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam leading prayer and whether he should lengthen it. The text says 'وينبغي للامام ان لا يطول بهم الصلوة' — it is befitting (recommended) for the imam not to prolong. The ruling is that shortening is mandub (recommended) and prolonging is makruh tanzihi.
2
Cite the primary dalil
The primary dalil is the hadith narrated by Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari where the Prophet ﷺ became angry at a man who lengthened the prayer and said: 'Whoever leads the people in prayer should be brief, for among them are the weak, the elderly, and the needy.'
Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command 'فليتجوز' is an imperative, but in Hanafi usul, it indicates recommendation (nadb) due to the context of consideration for the congregation. The Prophet himself sometimes lengthened, confirming it is not obligatory.
This shows the dalala is zanni in meaning.
4
Note the wisdom
The wisdom is to avoid hardship on the congregation, especially those who are weak, elderly, or have needs. The imam should be mindful of the congregation's condition.
This is a principle of raf' al-haraj (removal of difficulty).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينبغي للامام ان لا يطول بهم الصلوة : ۲۹ (۵۹) ويكره للنساء ان يصلين وحدهن بجماعة فان فعلن وقفت الامامة وسطهن كالعراة [۲۲۸] (۵۸) وينبغي للامام ان لا يطول بهم الصلوة : ۲۹ (۵۹) ويكره للنساء ان يصلين وحدهن بجماعة فان فعلن وقفت الامامة وسطهن كالعراة
And it is befitting for the imam not to prolong the prayer upon them. It is disliked for women that they pray alone in congregation; if they do, the female imam stands in their midst like naked people.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings. First, it is recommended for the imam to shorten the prayer so as not to inconvenience the congregation, especially the weak, elderly, and those with needs. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet ﷺ became angry at a man who lengthened the prayer, and said: 'Among you are some who cause aversion; whoever leads the people in prayer should be brief, for among them are the weak, the elderly, and the needy.' The Prophet also said: 'When one of you prays alone, he may lengthen as he wishes.' Thus, the ruling is that the imam should observe moderation, while the individual may lengthen. Second, it is disliked (makruh) for women to form a congregation with a female imam; if they do, the imam stands in the middle of the row, like the imam of naked men would stand. The reason is that women are commanded to stay behind men in prayer, and leading would put them forward, which is against proper conduct. Evidence is from the practice of Aisha and Umm Salama (may Allah be pleased with them).

Key Terms
يطول (yutawwil): To prolong the prayer, especially the recitation or bowing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the imam lengthening prayer?
A) It is wajib to shorten.
B) It is sunnah to lengthen.
C) It is makruh tanzihi to lengthen excessively.
D) It is haram to lengthen.

Key Takeaway
The imam should shorten prayer to avoid hardship on the congregation; prolonging is makruh tanzihi.

Women's Congregation with Female Imam
Ruling on women's congregation with female imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women forming a congregation with a female imam and describe the proper positioning.

Core Idea
It is makruh for women to form a congregation alone; if they do, the imam stands in the middle of the row.

The Hanafi school addresses the specifics of women's prayer congregation. While women may pray in congregation behind a male imam, forming a separate congregation with a female imam is disliked. If they do so, the female imam stands in the middle, not in front, to maintain modesty. This ruling is based on the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is women forming a congregation with a female imam. The text states 'يكره للنساء ان يصلين وحدهن بجماعة' — it is disliked (makruh). The hanafi position is that this is makruh tanzihi.
2
Understand the positioning
If they do pray, the imam stands in the middle of the row, not in front. The phrase 'كالعراة' (like naked people) indicates that standing in front would expose them, so they must stay in line.
Analogous to the ruling for naked men.
3
Examine the evidence
The evidence is from the practice of Aisha and Umm Salama (may Allah be pleased with them) who stood in the middle when leading women. This is a qawl sahabi (companion tradition).
No direct hadith is cited in this passage.

Women's Congregational Prayer and Imam's Position
Ruling on women's congregation and female imam's position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's congregational prayer, explain why it is makruh, and describe the position of the female imam.

Core Idea
Women leading women in prayer is permissible but disliked; the imam must stand in the middle, not in front.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on women forming their own congregation for salah. While permissible, it is considered makruh tanzihi due to the emphasis on women maintaining a low profile in the prayer rows. If performed, the female imam must stand in the middle of the row, analogous to the imam of naked men. The proof is drawn from the hadith on the best rows for women being the last, which discourages prominence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the specific act being ruled upon: women forming a congregation with a female imam. Note that the Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked, not haram).
The act is permissible in essence but disliked due to it placing women in a forward position.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith: 'The best rows for men are the first, and the worst are the last; the best rows for women are the last, and the worst are the first.' This indicates that women should not be prominent.
This hadith is ahad (single narration) but considered sahih.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophetic statement that the best rows for women are the last implies that women should avoid being in front. Leading a congregation inevitably places the imam ahead of others, contradicting this recommendation.
The Hanafi school uses this to derive dislike, not prohibition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers women's imamate for women permissible without dislike, citing general permission and the practice of Aisha (RA). Hanbalis also permit it.
This is a valid scholarly difference.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that women's congregation is makruh tanzihi. If performed, the imam must stand in the middle of the row, not in front.
This is from zahir al-riwayah and supported by later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره للنساء ان يصلين وحدهن بجماعة فان فعلن وقفت الامامة وسطهن كالعراة [۲۲۹] (۵۹) ويكره للنساء ان يصلين وحدهن بجماعة فان فعلن وقفت الامامة وسطهن كالعراة
It is disliked for women that they pray alone in congregation; if they do, the female imam stands in their midst like naked people.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage rules that it is makruh (disliked) for women to form a congregation with a female imam. However, if they do, the imam stands in the middle of the row, not in front, similar to how the imam of naked men stands in the middle. The reasoning is that women are commanded to stay behind men in prayer; leading would put them forward, which contradicts the recommended humility. Evidence includes the practice of Aisha and Umm Salama (may Allah be pleased with them), who led women from the middle. Also, the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ praising the last rows for women and the first for men indicates that women should avoid being prominent. Therefore, while permissible, it is makruh. The imam's position in the middle avoids drawing attention.

Key Terms
العراة (al-‘urāt): Plural of ‘ārī, meaning naked men. The analogy refers to the imam of naked men who must stand in the middle to avoid exposure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In front of the row, like men.
B) In the middle of the row.
C) Behind the row.
D) Anywhere she wishes.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, women may lead women in prayer, but it is makruh tanzihi, and the imam must stand in the middle of the row.

Positioning of a Single Follower on the Imam's Right
Ruling on the sunnah placement of one follower.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah position for one male follower in congregational prayer and identify the hadith evidence for it.

Core Idea
One male follower stands to the imam's right, slightly behind, as the Prophet did with Ibn Abbas.

In congregational prayer, the placement of followers is a sunnah that reflects the practice of the Prophet ﷺ. This lesson focuses on the ruling for a single male follower: he stands on the right side of the imam, not parallel but slightly behind. This is based on an authentic hadith and is agreed upon by all schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the positioning of one male follower in salah. Determine the hukm level from the text and the Hanafi school's classification.
The text simply says 'he has him stand on his right' – this indicates a sunnah act.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet moved him from the left to the right. Identify the type of evidence (Sunnah ahad).
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari, so thubut is qat'i but dalala is zanni regarding obligation.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action (placing Ibn Abbas on his right) demonstrates the specific placement. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action shows a sunnah, not a wajib.
The imperative form is not used, so the ruling is sunnah, not fard.
4
Note the cross-madhhab agreement
All four schools agree that one follower stands on the right. This makes it a muttafaq alayh ruling, though the precise position (slightly behind) may vary.
The text does not discuss differences, so we can note unanimous agreement.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
If you are praying with one male follower, gesture him to your right, slightly behind. This applies to the imam and the follower.
Be careful not to let the follower align exactly with the imam; he should be a little behind.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن صلى مع واحد اقامه عن يمينه [ ١٣١ وان كانا اثنين تقدمهما.
And whoever prays with one, he has him stand on his right. And if they are two, he precedes them.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage addresses the positioning of male followers in congregational prayer. If there is only one male follower, the imam makes him stand on his right side, slightly behind. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas (رضي الله عنهما) who prayed with the Prophet ﷺ and was placed on his right after originally standing on the left. The wisdom is that the right side is considered more honorable and facilitates the imam's supervision. The follower should not stand exactly parallel but slightly behind out of respect.

Key Terms
يمينه (yamīnihi): The right side of the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
One male follower stands on the imam's right, slightly behind, as a sunnah based on the Prophet's practice.

Positioning of Two Followers: Imam Stands Ahead
Ruling that with two followers, the imam stands ahead.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the imam's placement with two followers and explain the evidence from the hadith of Anas.

Core Idea
When two followers pray behind an imam, the imam stands ahead, not between them.

This lesson addresses a specific aspect of congregational prayer: where should the imam stand when there are exactly two followers? The Hanafi school, relying on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, holds that the imam leads from the front. However, a minority view within the school, attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf, suggests the imam stands between the two. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and why the majority opinion is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the specific action being ruled upon: the placement of the imam vis-à-vis two followers. The ruling is that it is sunnah (recommended) for the imam to stand ahead of them.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Anas ibn Malik (رضي الله عنه) reported in Sahih al-Bukhari and other collections. Anas prayed with an orphan behind the Prophet ﷺ, while Umm Sulaim stood behind them.
The hadith is mutawatir? Actually ahad but accepted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet ﷺ stood ahead of Anas and the orphan, demonstrating that the imam leads from the front when there are multiple followers. This establishes the placement.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf differed, holding that the imam should stand between the two followers, based on a report from Alqama and al-Aswad. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) prefer the hadith of Anas over the report cited by Abu Yusuf. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the imam stands ahead.
The hadith is stronger in transmission and practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كانا اثنين تقدمهما.
And if they are two, he precedes them.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This rule states that when there are two male followers, the imam stands ahead of them, and they form a row behind him. This is based on the hadith of Anas ibn Malik (رضي الله عنه) who prayed with an orphan behind the Prophet ﷺ, while his mother Umm Sulaim stood behind them. The practice confirms that two followers stand in a row behind the imam. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, held that the imam stands between the two followers, based on a report from Alqama and al-Aswad. But the relied-upon view (of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) is that the imam stands ahead, as it maintains the distinct position of leadership.

Key Terms
تقدمهما (taqaddamahumā): To precede them, i.e., the imam stands ahead of the two followers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Between them.
B) Ahead of them.
C) Behind them.
D) On their right side.

Key Takeaway
The imam leads from the front when there are two or more followers, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ.

Ruling on Women Leading Women and Imam's Position for the Naked
Ruling on women's imamah and positioning for naked worshippers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women leading women in prayer and explain why it is makruh, and identify the position of the imam for a congregation of naked worshippers.

Core Idea
Women's imamah is permissible but makruh; leading makes her stand forward, contradicting the sunna of women in back rows.

This lesson examines two specific rulings related to congregational prayer: the case of women leading other women, and the case of a naked congregation. Both rulings come with proofs from hadith and athar. Understanding the reasoning behind the dislike (karahah) in women's imamah requires careful attention to the hadith about row preferences, while the naked congregation's imam positioning is based on practice of the salaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their rulings
The passage first addresses women leading women in prayer, stating that the imam stands in the middle of the row, and then addresses a congregation of naked people, where the imam also stands in the middle. The commentary declares women's imamah as makruh.
The matn does not explicitly state the ruling for women's imamah; the commentary adds the hukm.
2
Locate the dalil for women's imamah
The commentary cites the hadith from Abu Huraira about best rows being first for men and last for women. It also cites an athar from Ali prohibiting women leading.
The hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith indicates that the best rows for women are the last, implying that women should not be forward. Since leading prayer requires being at the front, it contradicts the ideal, so it is disliked.
The reasoning is based on the concept that what is disliked for a woman (being forward) extends to the act of leading itself.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school generally permits women leading women without dislike, emphasizing the general permissibility of congregational prayer for women.
This ikhtilaf is based on different interpretations of the hadith and other evidence.
5
Understand the ruling for the naked congregation
For a group of people without clothing (e.g., shipwrecked), the imam stands in the middle of the row (not in front). They pray sitting and gesture for bowing and prostration, as per an athar from Qatada.
This ruling is specific to situations where covering is impossible; the imam's position avoids exposing private parts more than necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يصلين وحدهن بجماعة فان فعلن وقفت الامامة وسطهن كالعراة
عورت کی امامت مکروہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ حدیث ہے عن ابی هریرة قال قال رسول الله الا الله خير صفوف الرجال اولها وشرها آخرها و خير صفوف النساء آخرها و شرها اولها (مسلم شریف ، باب تسویۃ الصفوف واقامتها فضل الاول الخ ص ۱۸۲ نمبر ۴۴۰ را بو داؤد شریف، باب صف النساء والتاً خر عن الصف الاول ص ۰۶ انمبر ۶۷۸) جب عورت کو اگلی صف میں جانا مکروہ ہے تو امامت کرنا بھی مکروہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں آگے جانا ہوتا ہے۔ عورت کی امامت مکروہ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر بھی ہے۔ عن على قال لاتؤم المرأة (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، ۳۱۷ من کره ان توم المرأة النساء، ج اول ص ۴۳۰، نمبر ۴۹۵۷)
العراة : عاری کی جمع ہے ننگے۔ ننگے لوگوں کا امام درمیان میں کھڑا ہوگا اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن قتادة قال اذا خرج ناس من البحر عراة فامهم احدهم صلوا قعودا وكان امامهم معهم في النصف ويأمون ايماء (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب صلوۃ العریان ج ثانی ص۵۸۳، نمبر ۴۵۶۴)
They (women) pray alone in congregation, and if they do, the imam stands in their middle like the naked. The reason for women's imamah being makruh is this hadith: from Abu Huraira who said the Messenger of Allah said, 'Indeed the best rows of men are the first and the worst are the last, and the best rows of women are the last and the worst are the first.' (Muslim Sharif, Bab Taswiyat al-Sufuf, p. 182 no. 440; Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab Saff al-Nisa', p. 06 no. 678) When it is makruh for a woman to go to the front row, then to lead prayer is also makruh because it involves going forward. The imamah of women is makruh; another proof is this athar: from Ali who said, 'A woman should not lead prayer' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 317, man kariha an ta'umma al-mar'a al-nisa', vol. 1 p. 430, no. 4957). Al-Urata: plural of 'ari (naked). The imam of naked people will stand in the middle; its proof is this athar: from Qatada who said, 'When a group of people come out of the sea naked, and one of them leads them, they pray sitting, and their imam is with them in the middle, and they gesture (for bowing and prostration).' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Salat al-Uryan, vol. 2 p. 583, no. 4564)
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings with their proofs. First, regarding women leading women in prayer: the matn states that women pray in congregation alone, and the imam stands in their middle. The commentary explains that this is makruh (disliked) based on the hadith of Abu Huraira, which indicates that the best rows for women are the last, so leading which puts her forward is against the sunna. Additionally, an athar from Ali explicitly says that a woman should not lead prayer. Thus, while women may lead women, it is considered makruh. Second, regarding naked people (e.g., shipwrecked), the imam stands in the middle of the row, and they pray sitting while gesturing. This is proven by an athar from Qatada.

Key Terms
العراة (al-urata): Plural of 'ari, meaning naked persons who have no clothing to cover their private parts.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; an act that is blameworthy but not sinful; avoiding it is rewarded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a woman leading other women in prayer according to this text?
A) It is haram and invalid.
B) It is permissible but makruh.
C) It is mustahab.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Women may lead women in prayer, but this is disliked (makruh tanzihi) because leading places her forward, contrary to the sunna; the imam for a naked congregation stands in the middle.

Imam's Position with One Follower
Ruling on imam position with one follower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the imam's position with one follower and identify the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
With one follower, the imam stands ahead and the follower stands on his right, slightly behind.

This lesson addresses the proper positioning of the imam and a single follower in congregational prayer. The matn gives a concise rule, and the commentary expands using the hadith of Ibn Abbas. Understanding this positioning ensures the prayer follows the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states: 'Whoever prays with one person, he makes him stand on his right.' This is the Hanafi ruling for one follower.
2
Understand the positioning
The commentary clarifies that the follower stands on the imam's right but slightly behind, not directly beside him.
The imam remains ahead.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith of Ibn Abbas (ra) is cited: the Prophet (saw) placed Ibn Abbas from his left to his right, indicating the follower's position.
Bukhari no. 726.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن صلى مع واحد اقامه عن يمينه وان كانا اثنين تقدمهما.
اگر ایک آدمی کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے اس کو اپنی دائیں جانب کھڑا کرے۔ (1) دائیں جانب افضل ہے اس لئے ایک آدمی مقتدی ہو تو امام اس کو اپنی دائیں جانب میں کھڑا کرے(۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال صليت مع النبي لا لا لها ذات ليلة فقمت عن يساره فاخذ رسول الله الله برأسي من ورائي فجعلني عن یمینه فصلی (بخاری شریف، باب اذا قام الرجل عن یسار الامام وحوله الامام خلفہ الی یمینہ تمت صلوتہ ص ۱۰۰ نمبر ۷۲۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مقتدی ہو تو اس کو دائیں جانب کھڑا کرنا چاہئے۔ لیکن امام سے تھوڑا پیچھے کھڑا ہو گا۔
اگر دو مقتدی ہوں تو امام دونوں سے آگے کھڑا ہوگا۔
عن انس بن مالك قال صليت انا يتيم في بينا خلف النبى وامى خلفنا ام سلیم (بخاری شریف، باب المرأة وحدها تکون صفاص۱۰۱ نمبر ۷۲۷ ابو داؤد شریف، باب اذا کانوا ثلثۃ کیف یقومون ص ۹۷ نمبر ۱۲) اس حدیث میں انس اور یتیم دو آدمی تھے تو حضور کے پیچھے کھڑے ہوئے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو مقتدی ہوں تو امام آگے کھڑا ہوگا اور دونوں مقتدی پیچھے کھڑے ہونگے۔ نا امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک امام دونوں مقتدیوں کے بیچ میں کھڑا ہو گا۔ ان کا استدلال اس اثر سے ہے استاذن علقمة والاسود على عبد الله بن مسعود وقد كنا اطلنا القعود على بابه فخرجت الجارية فاستأذنت لهما فاذن لهما ثم قام فصلى بيني و بینه ثم قال هكذا رأيت رسول الله الله الله فعل (ابوداو د شریف، باب اذا کانوا ثلثۃ کیف یقومون ص ۹۷ نمبر ۶۱۳) اس حدیث میں عبداللہ بن مسعود علقمہ اور اسود کے درمیان کھڑے ہوئے ہیں۔ اس لئے امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یہ بہتر ہے۔ امام اعظم کے نزدیک یہ بھی جائز ہے لیکن آگے کھڑا ہونا بہتر ہے۔
And whoever prays with one person, he makes him stand on his right. And if they are two, he steps forward from them.
If he prays with one person, he makes him stand on his right. (1) The right side is better, so if there is one follower, the imam should make him stand on his right. (2) There is a hadith: from Ibn Abbas who said, 'I prayed with the Prophet one night and stood on his left, so the Messenger of Allah took my head from behind and made me stand on his right, then he prayed.' (Bukhari Sharif, Bab idha qama al-rajul 'an yasar al-imam, p. 100 no. 726) From this hadith it is understood that if there is one follower, he should be made to stand on the right. But he will stand slightly behind the imam.
If there are two followers, the imam will stand ahead of them.
From Anas ibn Malik who said, 'I and an orphan prayed in my house behind the Prophet, and my mother Umm Sulaym was behind us.' (Bukhari Sharif, Bab al-mar'a wahdaha takunu saffan, p. 101 no. 727; Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab idha kanu thalathah kayfa yaqumun, p. 97 no. 12) In this hadith, Anas and the orphan were two men, so they stood behind the Prophet. From this it is understood that if there are two followers, the imam stands ahead and both followers stand behind. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the imam will stand between the two followers. His evidence is this athar: Alqamah and al-Aswad sought permission from Abdullah ibn Masud, and we had been sitting at his door for a long time. Then a slave girl came out and asked permission for them, so he gave them permission. Then he stood and prayed between me and him, then said, 'Thus I saw the Messenger of Allah do.' (Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab idha kanu thalathah kayfa yaqumun, p. 97 no. 613) In this hadith, Abdullah ibn Masud stood between Alqamah and al-Aswad. Therefore, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, this is better. According to the Great Imam (Abu Hanifa), this is also permissible, but stepping forward is better.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage explains the position of the imam relative to the followers in congregational prayer. It is a ruling with proof, followed by an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states: with one follower, the imam makes him stand on his right; with two, the imam steps forward. The commentary provides hadith evidence: for one follower, the hadith of Ibn Abbas shows the follower stands on the imam's right but slightly behind. For two followers, the hadith of Anas shows the imam stands ahead and the followers behind. However, Imam Abu Yusuf differs regarding two followers: based on the action of Abdullah ibn Masud who stood between Alqamah and al-Aswad, he holds it is better for the imam to stand between them. The commentator notes that Abu Hanifa considers both positions permissible but stepping forward is better. Thus, the relied-upon position is that the imam steps forward when there are two followers.

Key Terms
یمین (yamin): Right side; the follower stands on the imam's right, slightly behind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where does a single follower stand relative to the imam?
A) Directly on the right, aligned.
B) On the right, slightly behind.
C) Directly behind.
D) On the left.

Key Takeaway
With one follower, the sunnah is for the follower to stand on the imam's right, slightly behind.

Imam's Position with Two Followers and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imam position with two followers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling for the imam's position with two followers and describe the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
For two followers, the majority view is the imam steps forward; Abu Yusuf says the imam stands between them, but stepping forward is better.

This lesson explores the positioning of the imam when there are two followers. The matn states the imam steps forward, but a hadith reported by Abdullah ibn Masud leads Imam Abu Yusuf to prefer the imam standing between the followers. Imam Abu Hanifa considers both permissible but gives preference to stepping forward. Understanding this dispute illustrates how Hanafi scholars weigh different hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The matn states: 'If they are two, he steps forward from them.' This is the majority Hanafi position.
2
Examine the hadith evidence for stepping forward
The hadith of Anas (ra) is cited: Anas and an orphan stood behind the Prophet (saw), showing the imam goes ahead.
Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
3
Examine the hadith evidence for standing between
Imam Abu Yusuf cites the action of Abdullah ibn Masud who stood between Alqamah and al-Aswad, citing the Prophet's practice.
Abu Dawud no. 613.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
Imam Abu Hanifa holds both positions permissible but considers stepping forward better. The relied-upon view is that the imam steps forward.
This tarjih is based on predominance of evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اگر ایک آدمی کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے اس کو اپنی دائیں جانب کھڑا کرے۔ (1) دائیں جانب افضل ہے اس لئے ایک آدمی مقتدی ہو تو امام اس کو اپنی دائیں جانب میں کھڑا کرے(۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال صليت مع النبي لا لا لها ذات ليلة فقمت عن يساره فاخذ رسول الله الله برأسي من ورائي فجعلني عن یمینه فصلی (بخاری شریف، باب اذا قام الرجل عن یسار الامام وحوله الامام خلفہ الی یمینہ تمت صلوتہ ص ۱۰۰ نمبر ۷۲۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مقتدی ہو تو اس کو دائیں جانب کھڑا کرنا چاہئے۔ لیکن امام سے تھوڑا پیچھے کھڑا ہو گا۔
اگر دو مقتدی ہوں تو امام دونوں سے آگے کھڑا ہوگا۔
عن انس بن مالك قال صليت انا يتيم في بينا خلف النبى وامى خلفنا ام سلیم (بخاری شریف، باب المرأة وحدها تکون صفاص۱۰۱ نمبر ۷۲۷ ابو داؤد شریف، باب اذا کانوا ثلثۃ کیف یقومون ص ۹۷ نمبر ۱۲) اس حدیث میں انس اور یتیم دو آدمی تھے تو حضور کے پیچھے کھڑے ہوئے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو مقتدی ہوں تو امام آگے کھڑا ہوگا اور دونوں مقتدی پیچھے کھڑے ہونگے۔ نا امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک امام دونوں مقتدیوں کے بیچ میں کھڑا ہو گا۔ ان کا استدلال اس اثر سے ہے استاذن علقمة والاسود على عبد الله بن مسعود وقد كنا اطلنا القعود على بابه فخرجت الجارية فاستأذنت لهما فاذن لهما ثم قام فصلى بيني و بینه ثم قال هكذا رأيت رسول الله الله الله فعل (ابوداو د شریف، باب اذا کانوا ثلثۃ کیف یقومون ص ۹۷ نمبر ۶۱۳) اس حدیث میں عبداللہ بن مسعود علقمہ اور اسود کے درمیان کھڑے ہوئے ہیں۔ اس لئے امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یہ بہتر ہے۔ امام اعظم کے نزدیک یہ بھی جائز ہے لیکن آگے کھڑا ہونا بہتر ہے۔
And whoever prays with one person, he makes him stand on his right. And if they are two, he steps forward from them.
If he prays with one person, he makes him stand on his right. (1) The right side is better, so if there is one follower, the imam should make him stand on his right. (2) There is a hadith: from Ibn Abbas who said, 'I prayed with the Prophet one night and stood on his left, so the Messenger of Allah took my head from behind and made me stand on his right, then he prayed.' (Bukhari Sharif, Bab idha qama al-rajul 'an yasar al-imam, p. 100 no. 726) From this hadith it is understood that if there is one follower, he should be made to stand on the right. But he will stand slightly behind the imam.

His evidence is this athar: Alqamah and al-Aswad sought permission from Abdullah ibn Masud, and we had been sitting at his door for a long time. (Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab idha kanu thalathah kayfa yaqumun, p. 97 no. 613) In this hadith, Abdullah ibn Masud stood between Alqamah and al-Aswad. Therefore, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, this is better. According to the Great Imam (Abu Hanifa), this is also permissible, but stepping forward is better.

Commentary
This passage explains the position of the imam relative to the followers in congregational prayer. It is a ruling with proof, followed by an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states: with one follower, the imam makes him stand on his right; with two, the imam steps forward. Key Terms
تقدم (taqaddum): To step forward; the imam stands ahead of the followers rather than in line with them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, where should the imam stand when there are two followers?
A) Between them.
B) Slightly ahead of them.
C) On the right of the first follower.
D) Behind them.

Key Takeaway
For two followers, the preferred Hanafi position is the imam stepping forward; standing between is also valid but less preferred.

Ruling: Men Cannot Follow a Woman or a Boy as Imam
Ruling that men cannot be led by a woman or a minor boy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding a man following a woman or a boy as imam, explain the dalil, and reconcile the Umm Waraqah hadith with the ruling.

Core Idea
A woman or boy cannot lead men in prayer; the follower's prayer is invalid.

This lesson examines a fundamental rule of congregational prayer: who can be an imam for men. The source text presents a clear prohibition and supports it with textual evidence and legal reasoning. We will unpack the proofs and address a potential counterargument from the hadith of Umm Waraqah.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the exact ruling: it is not permissible for men to follow a woman or a boy as imam. Note that the ruling applies to men, not to women following women.
The term 'la yajuz' indicates both prohibition and invalidity.
2
Find the dalil for women
Locate the hadith of Jabir: the Prophet forbade a woman leading a man. Understand that this is a clear, explicit command.
Hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi is cited.
3
Reconcile Umm Waraqah hadith
The hadith of Umm Waraqah seems to allow a woman leading her household. The source clarifies that she led only women, not men, based on combining narrations.
This reconciliation resolves the apparent contradiction.
4
Analyze the proof for boys
The reasoning is that a boy's prayer is not binding (nafl); he can break it without qada. The imam is a guarantor (jamin) for the follower's prayer. An invalid prayer cannot guarantee a valid one.
This is a qiyas: the boy's prayer is weak, so he cannot be a guarantor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز للرجال ان يقتدوا بامرأة او صبي.
نہیں جائز ہے مرد کے لئے کہ اقتدا کرے عورت کی یا بچے کی ۔
مرد مقتدی ہو اور اس کا امام عورت ہو یا بچہ ہوتو جائز نہیں ہے۔

اور بچے کی اقتدا اس لئے جائز نہیں کہ اس کی نماز ہی نہیں ہے۔ وہ نماز توڑ دے تو اس پر قضا نہیں ہے۔ اور امام مقتدی کی نماز کا ضامن ہوتا ہے اب امام کی نماز کمزور ہے تو مضبوط نماز کی ضامن وہ کیسے بن سکتی ہے۔ اس لئے بالغ مرد یا عورت کے لئے بچے کی اقتدا کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ عن الشعبي قال لايام الغلام حتى يحتلم (مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ۱۲۲ فی امامته الغلام قبل ان محکم ، ج اول ص ۳۰۶ نمبر ۳۵۰۵) عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله الله لا يتقدم الصف الاول اعرابي ولا عجمى ولا غلام لم يحتلم ( دارقطنی ، باب من
And it is not permissible for men to follow a woman or a boy. 
It is not permissible for a man to follow a woman or a boy. 
If a man is a follower and his imam is a woman or a boy, it is not permissible. 
In issue number 57, the hadith from Muslim no. 440 and Abu Dawud no. 678 has passed, which stated that the front row for women is bad and the back row is good. And due to leading prayer, she would be ahead of men, so for a man, her imamah is not valid. In issue 57, the issue of women's imamah that passed was that a woman can lead women, not men. (2) There is a hadith: from Jabir ibn Abdullah who said, 'I heard the Messenger of Allah say on his pulpit,' and he mentioned the hadith, and in it: 'Beware, a woman should not lead a man.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab la ya'tammu rajulun bi-imra'atin, vol. 3 p. 128, no. 5131) From this hadith, it is understood that a woman should not lead a man. In Abu Dawud Sharif, a hadith is narrated regarding women's imamah: from Umm Waraqah bint Abdullah ibn al-Harith, with this hadith, 'The Messenger of Allah used to visit her in her house, and he appointed a mu'adhdhin for her to give adhan, and he commanded her to lead the people of her household.' (Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab Imamah al-Nisa', p. 95 no. 592) This hadith indicates that a woman can lead prayer. But there is no proof in it that she led men. Combining Sunan al-Bayhaqi and other hadiths, it becomes clear that she led the women of her house, not men. 
And following a boy is not permissible because his prayer is not (valid). If he breaks his prayer, there is no qada upon him. And the imam is the guarantor of the follower's prayer; if the imam's prayer is weak, how can it be a guarantor for a strong prayer? Therefore, for an adult man or woman, following a boy is not valid. From al-Sha'bi: 'A boy should not lead until he reaches puberty.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 122, fi imamat al-ghulam qabla an yahlim, vol. 1 p. 306, no. 3505) From Ibn Abbas who said, 'The Messenger of Allah said: An Arab, a non-Arab, and an immature boy should not lead the first row.' (Darqutni, Bab man...
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling that men cannot pray behind a woman or an immature boy as imam. The commentary provides multiple proofs. For women: the hadith of Jabir explicitly forbids a woman leading a man. The hadith of Umm Waraqah, which seems to permit women leading, is clarified as applying only to leading women, not men. For boys: the reasoning is that a boy's prayer is not binding upon him (he can break it without making up), and the imam is responsible for the follower's prayer; thus a defective imam cannot guarantee a valid prayer. Additional athars from al-Sha'bi and a hadith from Ibn Abbas emphasize that an immature boy should not lead.

Key Terms
لا يجوز (la yajuz): Not permissible; indicates prohibition and invalidity of the act.
صبي (sabi): An immature minor boy who has not reached puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because a boy does not have knowledge of the rulings.
D) Because the boy is not allowed to stand in the first row.

Key Takeaway
A woman or an immature boy cannot lead men in prayer; their imamship invalidates the followers' prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Men May Not Pray Behind a Woman or a Boy
Ruling with proofs that men cannot follow a female or minor imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that men cannot follow a woman or a boy in congregational prayer and explain the primary textual evidence (dalil) and rational basis for this ruling.

Core Idea
A man's prayer behind a woman or a boy is invalid because the imam must have a valid obligatory prayer and be able to guarantee the follower's prayer.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position that men cannot follow a woman or a boy in congregational prayer. The matn states the ruling, and the commentary provides both textual evidence (hadith) and rational analogy (qiyas). Understanding the proofs strengthens your grasp of Hanafi imamate conditions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the precise ruling: It is not permissible for men to follow a woman or a boy as an imam in prayer. The prayer is invalid if done.
The ruling applies to fard prayers and is general.
2
Locate the primary dalil for the woman
The hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi: 'لا تؤمن امرأة رجلا' (A woman shall not lead a man). This is the direct textual evidence.
The hadith is ahad, so it is zanni al-thubut.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition ('la') indicates that the act is invalid. The imperative form implies prohibition in Hanafi usul.
The reason is that the woman would be ahead of the men, contradicting the recommended ranks.
4
Understand the rationale for the boy
The boy's prayer is not obligatory; he may break it without qada. Since the imam is responsible for the follower's prayer, a weak imam cannot guarantee a strong prayer.
This is based on qiyas: the imam must have a valid fard prayer.
5
Reconcile conflicting hadiths
The Umm Waraqa hadith is interpreted to mean she led only women, not men. Thus no contradiction.
This shows the method of jam' (reconciliation) between evidences.

It is not permissible for men to follow a woman or a boy. ... (Urdu commentary explaining hadiths and reasons).
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This is a ruling with proofs. The matn states that men cannot lead by a woman or a boy in prayer. The commentary provides evidence: hadiths prohibiting a woman leading a man (Sunan Bayhaqi) and indicating that a woman may lead only women (Umm Waraqa hadith). For a boy, the reasoning is that his prayer is not considered valid (he may break it without qada), and the imam is responsible for the followers' prayer; a weak imam cannot guarantee a strong prayer. There is also a discussion about the position of the imam relative to followers: Abu Yusuf prefers the imam standing between the followers, while Abu Hanifa allows standing ahead but considers it better. The commentary refutes the position of some scholars who allow a boy to lead by citing Hadith 'Let the men of understanding and reason lead you.'

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in prayer by a person who is not the imam (ma'mum).
امام (imam): The person who leads the prayer and is followed by others.
صبي (sabi): A male child who has not reached puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the boy must be circumcised

Key Takeaway
A man's prayer behind a woman or a boy is invalid; the imam must be a sane, adult male for the congregation of men.

The Recommended Row Order in Congregational Prayer
Ruling on the sequence of rows in congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of rows in congregational prayer and identify the category (sunnah muakkadah) of this ruling.

Core Idea
Rows in congregation: men first, then boys, then khuntha, then women—a recommended order from prophetic practice.

This lesson covers the ruling on arranging rows in congregational prayer. The Hanafi school prescribes a specific sequence based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). While not obligatory, following this order is a highly recommended sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Determine what act is being ruled upon: arranging rows in congregational prayer (saff).
2
State the Order
Recite the sequence: men first, then boys, then khuntha (ambiguous gender), then women.
The khuntha is placed between boys and women due to ambiguous status.
3
Understand the Rationale
The order is derived from prophetic practice, with men in front (best rows), women at back (best for them), and khuntha in between.
This respects modesty and maintains distinction.
4
Recognize the Hukm Level
Note that this order is sunnah muakkadah (highly recommended), not fard or wajib. The prayer remains valid if the order is different.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۳۳](٦٣) ويصف الرجال ثم الصبيان ثم الخنثى ثم النساء (۲۳۳] (۶۳) صف بنائی جائے گی مردوں کی پھر بچوں کی پھر خلفی کی پھر عورتوں کی۔ حدیث میں اسی طرح صف بنانے کا طریقہ بتایا گیا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن انس بن مالک قال صليت انا ويتيم في بيتنا خلف النبي الله و امى ام سلیم خلفنا ام سلیم (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب المرأة وحدها تكون صفاص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۷۲۷ ابوداؤد شریف، باب اذا کانوائلثۃ کیف یقومون ص ۹۷ نمبر ۶۱۲ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرد پہلے صف میں کھڑے ہونگے ۔ بچے دوسری صف میں اور خنثی چونکہ مرد اور عورت کے درمیان ہے اس لئے وہ عورت سے آگے اور بچوں سے پیچھے کھڑے ہونگے ۔ اور آخری صف میں عورت کھڑی ہوگی (۲) مسلم کی حدیث گزر چکی ہے عن ابی هریر قال قال رسول الله الا الله خير صفوف الرجال اولها وشرها آخرها وخير صفوف النساء آخرها و شرها اولها (و) (مسلم شریف، باب تسویۃ الصفوف دا قامتها فضل الاول فالاول ص ۱۸۲ نمبر ۴۴۰) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مرد کو آگے کھڑا ہونا چاہئے اور عورتوں کو پیچھے صف میں کھڑا ہونا چاہئے۔
Rows are arranged: men, then boys, then khuntha (hermaphrodite), then women. ... (Commentary explaining hadiths on row order).
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The matn specifies the order of rows in congregational prayer: men in front, then boys, then khuntha (people of ambiguous gender), then women at the back. The commentary supports this with a hadith from Anas ibn Malik where he, an orphan, and his mother Umm Sulaym prayed behind the Prophet: the men were in front, the boy (orphan) behind, and the woman at the back. Another hadith states: 'The best rows for men are the first, and the worst are the last; the best rows for women are the last, and the worst are the first.' The khuntha is placed between boys and women because of his/her ambiguous status.

Key Terms
خنثى (khuntha): A person with ambiguous sexual characteristics, neither clearly male nor female.
صف (saff): A row in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Women, then children, then men
B) Men, then boys, then khuntha, then women
C) Men, then women, then children
D) Boys, then men, then women

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends arranging rows: men first, then boys, then khuntha, then women, based on prophetic practice.

Prophetic Evidence for the Order of Rows
Evidence from hadith for row order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two hadiths used as evidence and explain how each supports the Hanafi order of rows.

Core Idea
The hadith of Anas shows the actual arrangement; the hadith of Abu Hurairah gives a general principle supporting the order.

This lesson delves into the hadith evidence that forms the basis for the Hanafi ruling on row arrangement. Understanding the proofs strengthens your knowledge of how rulings are derived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the First Hadith
Locate the hadith of Anas ibn Malik in the text. Note the arrangement: Prophet in front, Anas and orphan behind him, Umm Sulaym behind them.
This is a practical demonstration of row order.
2
Extract the Ruling from the First Hadith
From this hadith, deduce that men (Anas was an adult) stand in front, boys (orphan) next, and women (Umm Sulaym) at the back.
The khuntha is not mentioned here, but by analogy, as an ambiguous person, they are placed between boys and women.
3
Identify the Second Hadith
The hadith of Abu Hurairah states: 'The best rows for men are the first, and the worst are the last; the best rows for women are the last, and the worst are the first.'
This provides a general principle: men's best is front, women's best is back.
4
Apply the Principle to the Khuntha
Since the khuntha is not clearly male or female, they should be placed between the groups, following the general rule that they are neither in the best rows of men nor in the best rows of women.
Thus the order is established: men, then boys, then khuntha, then women.

[۲۳۳](٦٣) ويصف الرجال ثم الصبيان ثم الخنثى ثم النساء (۲۳۳] (۶۳) صف بنائی جائے گی مردوں کی پھر بچوں کی پھر خلفی کی پھر عورتوں کی۔ حدیث میں اسی طرح صف بنانے کا طریقہ بتایا گیا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن انس بن مالک قال صليت انا ويتيم في بيتنا خلف النبي الله و امى ام سلیم خلفنا ام سلیم (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب المرأة وحدها تكون صفاص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۷۲۷ ابوداؤد شریف، باب اذا کانوائلثۃ کیف یقومون ص ۹۷ نمبر ۶۱۲ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرد پہلے صف میں کھڑے ہونگے ۔ بچے دوسری صف میں اور خنثی چونکہ مرد اور عورت کے درمیان ہے اس لئے وہ عورت سے آگے اور بچوں سے پیچھے کھڑے ہونگے ۔ اور آخری صف میں عورت کھڑی ہوگی (۲) مسلم کی حدیث گزر چکی ہے عن ابی هریر قال قال رسول الله الا الله خير صفوف الرجال اولها وشرها آخرها وخير صفوف النساء آخرها و شرها اولها (و) (مسلم شریف، باب تسویۃ الصفوف دا قامتها فضل الاول فالاول ص ۱۸۲ نمبر ۴۴۰) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مرد کو آگے کھڑا ہونا چاہئے اور عورتوں کو پیچھے صف میں کھڑا ہونا چاہئے۔
Rows are arranged: men, then boys, then khuntha (hermaphrodite), then women. ... (Commentary explaining hadiths on row order).
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The matn specifies the order of rows in congregational prayer: men in front, then boys, then khuntha (people of ambiguous gender), then women at the back. The commentary supports this with a hadith from Anas ibn Malik where he, an orphan, and his mother Umm Sulaym prayed behind the Prophet: the men were in front, the boy (orphan) behind, and the woman at the back. Another hadith states: 'The best rows for men are the first, and the worst are the last; the best rows for women are the last, and the worst are the first.' The khuntha is placed between boys and women because of his/her ambiguous status.

Key Terms
خنثى (khuntha): A person with ambiguous sexual characteristics, neither clearly male nor female.
صف (saff): A row in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Hadith of Anas ibn Malik
C) Hadith of Ibn Abbas
D) Hadith of Aisha

Key Takeaway
Two hadiths form the primary evidence: the Anas hadith shows the physical arrangement, and the Abu Hurairah hadith provides the general principle.

Woman Next to Man Invalidates His Prayer
Ruling on invalidation of man's prayer when woman stands adjacent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions under which a man's prayer is invalidated when a woman stands adjacent to him, and explain why this ruling is contrary to qiyas (khilaf al-qiyas).

Core Idea
A woman standing next to a man invalidates his prayer only when five specific conditions are met — a rare exception (khilaf al-qiyas) based on hadith.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Saghir presents a unique Hanafi ruling: if a woman stands next to a man during a congregational prayer and he intends to lead her, his prayer becomes invalid. While this might seem harsh, the commentary explains that it is an exception to analogy (khilaf al-qiyas) and is strictly conditioned. By understanding these conditions, you will appreciate the precision of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a man and woman praying together in the same row. The ruling is that the man's prayer becomes invalid (fasid/batil).
Note that only the man's prayer is affected; the woman's prayer remains valid.
2
Recognize the exceptional nature (khilaf al-qiyas)
The commentary states this ruling is contrary to qiyas, meaning it cannot be derived by analogy and is based solely on explicit textual evidence (hadith). This emphasizes that the ruling is strict and limited.
This is a reminder that some Hanafi rulings are text-based exceptions that do not extend to other cases.
3
List the five conditions for invalidation
Work through each condition: (1) both are in the same prayer, (2) no barrier between them, (3) the prayer includes ruku' and sujud (not janazah), (4) the woman is of desirable age, (5) the man intends to lead her (he is the imam).
All conditions must be met; if any is missing, the prayer remains valid.
4
Understand the consequence
When all conditions are met, the man's prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated. The woman's prayer is not affected.
The invalidation is specific to the man's prayer; the woman's prayer remains valid regardless.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school does not rule invalidation; they consider it makruh (disliked). This is a mukhtalaf fih issue.
The practical difference is that in the Shafi'i school, the prayer is valid but disliked, while Hanafis require repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۳۴] (۶۴) فان قامت امرأة الى جنب رجل وهما مشتركان في صلوة واحدة فسدت صلوته. عورت مرد کی بغل میں کھڑی ہو جائے اس سے مرد کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے یہ خلاف قیاس ہے۔ اس لئے فاسد ہونے کے لئے چند شرطیں ہیں (۱) دونوں کی نماز ایک ہو (۲) بغیر پردہ کے عورت کھڑی ہو (۳) رکوع اور سجدہ والی نماز ہو (۴) عورت اہل شہوت ہو (۵) اور امام نے اس کی امامت کی نیت کی ہو تب مرد کی نماز فاسد ہوگی۔ کی مرد
If a woman stands next to a man and they are both participating in one prayer, his prayer becomes invalid. ... (Conditions for invalidation).
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The matn states that if a woman stands adjacent to a man in the same prayer, the man's prayer becomes invalid. The commentary explains that this is contrary to qiyas (analogy) and lists five conditions for invalidation: 1) Both are praying the same prayer; 2) The woman stands without a barrier; 3) The prayer includes ruku' and sujud (i.e., not janazah); 4) The woman is one who is usually desired (i.e., of age); 5) The man intends to lead her in prayer (i.e., he is the imam). Only if all conditions are met does the man's prayer become invalid. The text ends abruptly, but the conditions are given.

Key Terms
فسدت صلوته (fasadat salatuhu): His prayer becomes invalid.
خلاف قياس (khilaf al-qiyas): Contrary to analogy; the ruling is an exception based on hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whenever a woman stands near him in any prayer
B) Only if the woman is his mahram
C) When five conditions are met, including the prayer having ruku' and sujud and the man being the imam
D) Only if the woman touches the man

Key Takeaway
A man's prayer is invalidated only when five specific conditions are met, making this a strictly circumscribed exception to the default rule of validity.

Invalidation of Man's Prayer When Woman Stands Beside Him
Ruling on invalidation of prayer due to woman's adjacency, with conditions and inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on invalidation of a man's prayer when a woman stands next to him, identify the conditions, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A man's prayer is invalid if a woman of desire prays directly beside him without a barrier in the same obligatory prayer.

This lesson examines a controversial Hanafi ruling that differs from other schools. The source text presents the ruling, its conditions, and the proofs from athar of Ibrahim and the instruction of Umar. We will analyze the Hanafi position and the Shafi'i objection, learning to distinguish between valid scholarly differences and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and conditions
Identify the ruling: the man's prayer becomes fasid (invalid). List the five conditions: same prayer, no barrier, prayer includes ruku and sujud, woman is ahl al-shahwah, and the iman intended her imamate (or man being imam).
The fifth condition is ambiguous; primary conditions are the first four.
2
Identify the Hanafi proofs
Note the athar of Ibrahim reported by Abu Hanifa: 'When a woman prays next to a man... his prayer is invalid.' Also the athar of Harith ibn Muawiyah where Umar advised using a barrier, implying invalidation without it.
These are narrations from the salaf, not direct Quran or Sunnah.
3
Understand the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is only makruh, not invalid. His proof is the hadith of Aisha: she slept in front of the Prophet while he prayed voluntary prayer, and he touched her, yet the prayer remained valid.
This is a direct hadith, which appears stronger at first glance.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi school distinguishes: Aisha's hadith pertains to voluntary prayer (tatawwu'), not obligatory. The ruling applies to obligatory prayers. Also, there may have been an implicit barrier.
Thus the general rule for obligatory prayers is preserved.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi, the man's prayer is invalid and must be repeated. Under Shafi'i, it remains valid (only disliked). This affects congregational prayers where the imam's prayer may be invalid, affecting the followers.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position as stated by Muhammad al-Shaybani.

بمحاذاة النساء ج رابع ص ۲۵۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت اور مرد کے درمیان پردہ ہو تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی (۴) اخبـرنـا ابـو حنيفة عن حماد عن ابرهيم قال اذا صلت المرأة الى جانب الرجل وكانا في صلوة انها قالت كنت انام بين يدى رسول الله له ورجلائي في قبلته فاذا سجد غمزنی فقبضت رجلی فاذا قام بسطتها ( بخاری شریف ، باب التطوع خلف المرأة ص ۷۳ ، نمبر ۵۱۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت محاذات میں آجائے Then if a woman stands next to a man and they are partners in one prayer, his prayer becomes invalid. If a woman stands next to a man, then the man's prayer becomes invalid. This is against analogy (qiyas). Therefore, there are several conditions for invalidation: (1) Both are in the same prayer. (2) The woman stands without a barrier. (3) The prayer includes bowing and prostration. (4) The woman is of desire (i.e., adult and attractive). (5) The man intends to lead her? (Text ambiguous, but the condition from earlier is that the imam intended her imamate). Then the man's prayer becomes invalid. Because the man should have advised the woman to move back, but he did not, so his prayer is invalid. (2) In ruling no. 63, the hadith of Muslim passed: the last row is better for women, but she came forward, so she acted against the sunnah, thus his prayer is invalid. (3) From al-Harith ibn Muawiyah that he rode to Umar ibn al-Khattab asking about three matters. He came to Medina and Umar asked: Why have you come? He said: To ask about three matters. Umar said: What are they? He said: Sometimes I and my wife are in a narrow space, and prayer time comes. If I pray and she is alongside me, and if she prays behind me she would exit the building. He said: Place a cloth as a screen between you and her, then pray alongside [i.e., beside the barrier] if you wish. (Meaning from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on man and woman praying one alongside the other, vol. 2 p. 36 no. 2391; Majma al-Zawaid vol. 1 p. 76; I'la al-Sunan, chapter on invalidation of man's prayer due to woman's adjacence, vol. 4 p. 252). This athar shows that if there is a barrier between man and woman, the prayer is not invalidated. (4) Abu Hanifa informed us from Hammad from Ibrahim that he said: When a woman prays next to a man and both are in one prayer, his prayer becomes invalid. Muhammad said: And we take this [view], and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa. (Kitab al-Athar of Imam Muhammad, chapter on what cuts off prayer, p. 27 no. 137). This athar shows that the fatwa of Ibrahim was that if man and woman stand together without a barrier, the man's prayer becomes invalid. Benefit: Imam al-Shafi'i says that a woman standing next to a man is makruh but the prayer is not invalidated. His evidence is the hadith of Aisha, wife of the Prophet, that she said: I used to sleep in front of the Messenger of Allah, and my feet were in the direction of his qibla. When he prostrated, he would poke me and I would pull back my feet, and when he stood up I would stretch them out. (Bukhari, chapter on voluntary prayer behind a woman, p. 73 no. 513). This hadith shows that if a woman comes in line, the prayer is not invalidated, because the Prophet used to touch Aisha during prayer and the prayer remained valid.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage contains the ruling (hukm) that if a woman stands next to a man in the same obligatory prayer, the man's prayer becomes invalid (fasid) according to the Hanafi school. This is contrary to qiyas, so conditions are specified: both must be in the same prayer, no barrier, prayer includes ruku and sujud, the woman is of desire (i.e., adult and potentially tempting), and the man is the imam? The text says 'and the imam intended her imamate' but the application seems to be for the man who leads. The commentary provides evidence: the athar of Harith ibn Muawiyah where Umar advised using a barrier, showing that without a barrier the prayer would be invalid. The athar from Ibrahim through Abu Hanifa explicitly states the ruling. A benefit (faida) records the Shafi'i position that it is only makruh, not invalid, citing the hadith of Aisha. The Hanafi response distinguishes the context: Aisha's hadith was about voluntary prayer or there was an implicit barrier, and the general ruling remains for obligatory prayers with a woman of desire. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the man's prayer is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Terms
محاذات (muḥādhāt): Standing alongside or adjacent to someone in prayer, within the same row.
فاسد (fāsid): Invalid; the act is legally deficient and must be repeated or compensated.
أهل شهوة (ahl al-shahwah): A woman who is adult and physically desirable, capable of inciting desire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The prayer is a voluntary (nafl) prayer.
D) There is no barrier (sutrah) between them.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a man's prayer is invalid if a woman of desire stands directly beside him without a barrier in the same obligatory prayer, based on athar of Ibrahim, while the Shafi'i school disagrees based on a hadith of Aisha.

Women's Attendance in Congregational Prayer: Ruling and Reasoning
Ruling with proof on women's congregational attendance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's attendance in congregational prayer, identify the conditions that change the ruling, and explain the reasoning based on fitna and the Prophetic permission.

Core Idea
A woman's attendance in congregational prayer is permissible but disliked for young women due to the risk of fitna.

In this passage, the author presents the Hanafi ruling that it is makruh for women to attend congregational prayer. However, this is not an absolute prohibition; the reasoning reveals a nuanced position: the act is fundamentally permissible based on the Prophet's permission, but it becomes disliked for young women due to the potential for fitna (temptation) that may arise from mixing with men. The passage also alludes to a hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that suggests a stricter view in later times, though the text is cut off.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is women attending congregational prayer. The ruling is 'makruh' (disliked).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The Prophet's (ﷺ) permission for women to attend the mosque, and an incomplete hadith of Aisha.
The permission establishes permissibility; Aisha's hadith suggests further restrictions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof lead to the ruling? The Prophet's permission indicates ibaha (permissibility). However, the potential for fitna overrides this permissibility for young women, making it makruh tanzih.
4
Note the distinction
Does the text differentiate? It specifically says 'young women' are makruh, implying elderly women are not subject to this dislike.
This distinction is crucial for proper application.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
What is the operative ruling? For young women, it is makruh tanzih; for elderly women, it is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره للنساء حضور الجماعة. عورتوں کے لئے جماعت میں حاضر ہونا مکروہ ہے۔ وجه (۱) عورتوں کو مسجد کی جماعت میں شامل ہونا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور نے اجازت دی ہے۔ لیکن جوان عورتوں کے لئے مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ مردوں کے ساتھ اختلاط سے فتنہ کا خطرہ ہے (۲) سمعت عائشه زوج النبي لا تقول لو ان رسول الله له رأى ما احدث
And it is disliked for women to attend the congregation. It is disliked for women to attend the congregation. Reason: (1) It is permissible for women to join the mosque congregation because the Prophet gave permission. But for young women it is makruh because the risk of fitna (temptation) due to mixing with men. (2) I heard Aisha, the wife of the Prophet, say: If the Messenger of Allah had seen what innovations women have introduced...
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that women's attendance in congregational prayer is makruh (disliked). The commentary explains that the permissibility is established, but for young women it becomes makruh due to the fear of fitna from mixing with men. The second point begins a hadith of Aisha suggesting that later innovations would lead to a stricter ruling, but the text is cut off. The Hanafi ruling is that while elderly women may attend, young women should avoid it.

Key Terms
مكروه (makrūh): Disliked; an act that is not sinful but best avoided.
فتنة (fitna): Temptation, trial, or disorder, particularly sexual temptation due to mixing genders.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits women's mosque attendance in principle but recommends against it for young women to avoid fitna.

beginner

Women Attending Congregational Prayer: The Hanafi Ruling
Stating the ruling with brief explanatory commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women attending congregational prayer, distinguishing between young and old women, and explain the rationale of fitnah.

Core Idea
Women's attendance at congregational prayer is permissible in principle but makruh for young women due to fitnah risk.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on women attending congregational prayers. The matn states that it is makruh for women, but the commentary clarifies that this is not absolute: it is permissible based on prophetic permission, yet makruh for young women to avoid fitnah. Understanding the balance between permission and prevention is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being discussed? (women attending congregational prayer) What is the explicit ruling given in the matn? (makruh)
The matn is concise; the ruling is stated without qualification initially.
2
Note the distinction in the commentary
The commentary explains that the ruling is not absolute. It mentions that it is 'ja'iz' (permissible) due to the Prophet's permission, but then specifies that for young women it is makruh due to fear of fitnah.
The distinction between young and old women is crucial.
3
Analyze the basis for the ruling
Identify the two elements: permission from the Prophet (as evidence for permissibility) and the fear of fitnah (as the operative cause for makruh).
Fitnah (temptation, disorder) overrides the general permission.
4
Recognize the incomplete hadith
The passage begins quoting Aisha but is cut off. Understand that while the hadith supports the cautious approach, the primary basis is the fitnah rationale.
The incomplete text does not change the ruling derived from the clear statement.

Commentary
Passage type: ruling statement (matn). The text states the basic ruling that it is makruh for women to attend congregational prayer. The commentary (wajh) explains that the ruling is not absolute: it is permissible for women to go to the mosque for jama'ah based on the Prophet's permission, but for young women it is makruh due to the risk of fitnah from mixing with men. The second point quotes a hadith of Aisha about the Prophet's hypothetical prohibition, but the text is cut off. The ruling discourages women's attendance while acknowledging its basic permissibility.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; here it refers to a prohibition without being haram, likely makruh tahrimi due to the fitnah risk.

Old Women Attending Mosque: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on permissibility for old women to attend mosque for specific prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which prayers an old woman may attend in congregation and explain the intra-Hanafi difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
An old woman may attend the mosque for Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha; the Sahibayn extend it to all prayers.

This passage addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of elderly women attending congregational prayers. While both sides agree on the basic permissibility due to reduced fitnah, they differ on which prayers are included. Understanding this difference requires careful attention to the underlying reasons (ta'lil) and the textual evidence cited.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling: it is permissible for an old woman to go out for Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha prayers only.
The term 'la ba's' indicates permissibility (ibaha).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) disagree, holding that it is permissible for all five daily prayers.
Sahibayn consider the low fitnah risk sufficient for all times.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Sahibayn's reasoning: old women have reduced desire and thus pose minimal fitnah at any prayer time.
They rely on the general absence of fitnah rather than specific hadith.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
See how Abu Hanifa counters: he cites the hadith that evil people are asleep at Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha, and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud restricting permission to those times.
The Hanafi response prioritises caution and specific textual evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, an old woman may not attend Zuhr or Asr congregation; under Sahibayn, she may.
The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa's more restrictive view.

[236] (66) There is no harm in the old woman going out for Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is permissible for the old woman to go out for all prayers. (Evidence) ... The women of the Companions: the Prophet forbade them, so why not prevent the women of today? (3) From Abdullah from the Prophet, he said: A woman's prayer in her house is better than her prayer in her room, and her prayer in her closet is better than her prayer in her house. (Reference) From this hadith it is known that praying in the mosque is permissible, but praying at home is better, and this is evidence for the makruh of going to the mosque. Evidence for going to the mosque: from Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah said: Do not prevent the female servants of Allah from the mosques of Allah, but let them go out without fragrance. [236] (66) There is no harm in old women going to the mosque for Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the two companions (Sahibayn) said that it is permissible for old women to go out for all prayers. The reasoning: Old women have less desire, and especially at Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha, evil people are asleep, so it is permissible for them to go to the mosque for congregational prayer. The two companions said that because old women have less desire, they may go for all prayers. Evidence: the hadith: No woman who applies perfume should attend the Isha prayer with us. From this it is known that a woman who has desire should not attend the mosque. Another athar from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: By the One besides whom there is no god, no woman has prayed a prayer better than the prayer she prays in her house, except if it is the Masjid al-Haram or the Masjid of the Messenger, except an old woman in her socks. From this athar it is known that an old woman, even without perfume and with a simple garment, may go to the mosque. Some who permit women to go to the mosque argue from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Do not prevent your women from the mosques if they ask your permission. Then Bilal ibn Abdullah said: By Allah, we will prevent them. Footnotes: (a) If the Prophet had seen what women have innovated today, he would have prevented them from the mosques, as the women of Bani Isra'il were prevented. (b) The Prophet said: A woman's prayer in her house is better than her prayer in her room, and her prayer in her closet is better than her prayer in her house. (c) The Prophet said: No woman who applies perfume should come to the Isha prayer with us. (d) Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: By Allah, no woman has prayed a better prayer than the one she prays in her house, except in the Masjid al-Haram or the Masjid of the Messenger, except an old woman who comes in her socks without fragrance. (e) The Prophet said: Do not prevent your women... (continues on next page).
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
Passage type: intra-Hanafi dispute. This passage discusses the permissibility of old women attending congregational prayers in the mosque. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is permissible (la ba's) only for Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha prayers, because at those times evil people are asleep, reducing the risk of fitnah. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) extend this to all prayers, reasoning that old women have less physical attractiveness and desire, so the risk is minimal in all prayers. The text then provides supporting evidence: a hadith prohibiting perfumed women from attending Isha, implying that an old woman without perfume may attend. Another athar from Ibn Mas'ud states that a woman's prayer at home is best except for old women who may go to the mosque. Footnotes elaborate that if the Prophet saw modern women's behavior, he would forbid them, and that prayer at home is superior in general. The passage clarifies that the permission is conditional on lack of fitnah and modesty.

Key Terms
العجوز (al-'ajuz): An old woman who has passed the age of desire and attractiveness.
صاحبین (sahibayn): The two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, major disciples of Abu Hanifa.

D) Only Zuhr and Asr.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that an old woman may attend only Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha congregation, provided she avoids perfume and adornment.
